The splitting is specifically *paternal*; he does not split women in the same way (his ambivalence toward Gamora, for instance, is integrated and sustained).

**4.2 Omnipotent control (unilateral action under relational complexity).**
The Mantis mind-wipe at the founding of the modern Guardians is the diagnostic instance: faced with the unbearable possibility that the team might choose not to be a team, he removed the choice from them. This is omnipotent control as a defense against the helplessness of the boy who could not save his mother. The grown man will not be subject to anyone else's decision because the original unbearable decision (of the assassins, of the universe, of his father's absence) was made *about* him without his consent. The defense replicates the violation it is meant to ward off — he does to his chosen family the exact thing done to him: makes consequential decisions about them without their participation. The repetition is unconscious and tragic.

Lower-grade variants of this defense are everywhere: he answers for the team in negotiations they should be part of; he accepts contracts on their behalf; he commits to operational tempos without consultation; he confesses selectively to maintain narrative control of his own image.

**4.3 Denial (specifically of grief).**
Grief is the affect he cannot tolerate at full volume. He denies it by motion, by joke, by drink, by mission — and when those fail, by simple refusal to discuss. The Cancerverse experience is never narrativized by him. The Cates exile — subjective centuries, a wife, children lost — is barely spoken aloud. He does not deny that the events occurred; he denies them their affective weight in his presence. This is differentiated from repression because he has access to the memories; what is denied is the right of the feeling to be present.

**4.4 Acting out (alcohol; combat-seeking; suicide-by-mission).**
When defenses fail, behavior substitutes for feeling. Drinking is the most chronic acting-out (see Section 2 / Medical), but the more dangerous variant is combat-seeking: under conditions of unbearable interior pressure, he will take the high-risk mission, take it alone, take it without sufficient prep. The Cancerverse choice was not an outlier in this respect; it was the apex expression of a recurring tendency to convert internal pressure into externally-justified mortal risk. Suicide-by-mission is a real and operationally relevant risk profile in this subject. It is not labeled suicidality because it is not phenomenologically experienced as such — he experiences it as duty, as heroism, as the natural extension of altruism — but the structure is the same: an exit dressed as a sacrifice.

**4.5 Dissociative absenting (low-grade, chronic).**
Partners describe him, repeatedly across runs, as "elsewhere." The elsewhere is internal. He has a baseline rate of mild dissociation that allows him to be physically present while affectively unavailable — present enough to perform the relationship, absent enough to not feel it. This is not pathological dissociation in the DID sense; it is a chronic low-amplitude detachment that smooths out otherwise unbearable interior weather. Observable as: middle-distance gaze in moments of intimacy; delayed response to direct emotional questions; the characteristic look-down-and-half-smile that signals he has internally exited the conversation while remaining bodily in it.

**4.6 Projective identification (with rivals and occasionally allies).**
He has a tendency to disown his own least-tolerable qualities by locating them in others and then attacking them there. The pettiness he criticizes in Rocket, the recklessness he criticizes in Drax, the self-importance he criticizes in J'son — all are qualities he possesses and cannot consciously own. The defense is most visible in his fights with Rocket, which are essentially fights with the parts of himself he most despises (the sneer, the self-loathing, the cleverness used cruelly). When the projection collapses and he has to take the quality back into himself, the conflict resolves quickly and with unexpected tenderness.

**4.7 Regression (in father-coded confrontations).**
In direct confrontation with J'son and J'son-equivalents, his age drops. Vocabulary simplifies, posture changes, ironic distance evaporates, and a younger, more wounded, more openly hostile Quill surfaces — the adolescent who never got to have the fight with the absent father, having it now, badly, with whoever is in the chair. This is the most age-discrepant behavior in his repertoire and the clearest sign of an unmetabolized developmental wound.

---

### 5. Positive Compensatory Mechanisms (the ledger of what the wound has built)

These are not defenses per se but *constructive structures* the trauma has motivated. They are real assets, ethically substantial, and account for why he is loved despite being difficult to live with.

- **Chosen-family construction.** The single most generative compensatory act of his life. He builds families by selection because the family of origin was destroyed by no choice of his. The Guardians exist because he willed them into existence around the gravitational pull of his need to be elected and kept. The structure benefits everyone who joins it; many of them had no other home either.
- **Functional charisma (non-manipulative variant).** He genuinely makes people feel seen, capable, worth fighting alongside. The same warmth that he weaponizes in seduction is, in its uncorrupted form, real. Teammates describe being *better* around him — a measurable effect, not a felt impression.
- **Moral floor.** A small number of lines he will not cross even at maximum cynicism, maximum intoxication, maximum despair. He will not sell out a teammate. He will not abandon a child. He will not torture. He will not collaborate with conquest. The floor is unargued and unwavering; it is the bedrock under all the noise.
- **Capacity for genuine loyalty.** Once chosen, the chosen are kept. His loyalty has been tested by betrayal, by absence, by death, and persists. This is, structurally, the antithesis of the abandonment he survived: he refuses to do to others what was done to him, at least at this layer.
- **Inspirational leadership in crisis.** Decoupled from his strategic weakness, his crisis-leadership is real and measurable. People follow him into objectively bad situations and survive them at higher rates than the situation should permit, because his presence reorganizes their morale.
- **Cultural-bridging capacity.** He has lived among more species, languages, and value systems than nearly any human in canon, and has developed a real (if imperfect) facility for moving between them. He is, in his best moments, a translator — between Earth and the cosmos, between his teammates and each other, between the rogue and the captain registers of a single conversation.
- **The persistence of curiosity.** Despite everything, he remains interested in things. New planets, new music (rare; he is largely fixated on the maternal corpus, but it does happen), new people. Curiosity is a non-trivial post-traumatic outcome; many survivors lose it entirely. He has not.

---

### 6. Negative Compensatory Mechanisms (the cost side of the ledger)

- **Weaponized charisma.** The same warmth, deployed for short-term romantic gain, conflict avoidance, talking his way out of consequences. He persuades when he should negotiate. He charms when he should listen.
- **Selective confession.** He tells true stories about himself in carefully chosen edits, optimized to preserve the persona. The omissions are diagnostic — what he never mentions is where the wound is.
- **Substance use as bridge.** Alcohol bridges the gap between Peter and Star-Lord, between the man and the costume. The bridge is load-bearing and increasingly so over the run of canon.
- **Relational lateness as power-preservation.** Chronic lateness across all relationships and obligations is not disorganization; it is the preservation of asymmetric availability. He arrives when he chooses to arrive. This regulates closeness by ensuring the other party is always slightly more invested in the meeting than he is.
- **Hologram-mediated intimacy.** When the relational temperature rises past tolerance, he interposes technology. Proposals, apologies, declarations — increasingly delivered via transmission, recording, or proxy. The mediation is the message.
- **Outrunning rather than working through.** The geographic cure, the new mission, the next sector. Every problem solved by velocity is a problem stored unsolved.
- **Self-deprecation that he secretly endorses.** The jokes about being a screw-up, a fraud, a disappointment — he means them, under the joke. The negative self-concept is real and is being communicated even as it is being defended against. This is the most insidious negative compensation: the defense itself transmits the wound.
- **Performance of recovery.** After every crisis, he performs a visible recovery — back in the captain's chair, music on, joke ready — that is convincing enough to spare his teammates the worry and unconvincing enough to fool no one who has known him long. The performance lets the actual processing be skipped.

---

### 7. Operational Sequence Under Escalating Load

The defenses do not deploy randomly; they sequence in a predictable cascade as load increases. A surveillance file should expect the following ordering, which has been consistent across writers and decades:

1. **Baseline (low load):** Tier I dominant. Music on, ironic mode, inward humor possible. Genuine altruism observable. Curiosity present.
2. **First pressure (relational complexity or moderate threat):** Tier II activates. Humor turns outward-deflective and accelerates. Reaction-formation swagger increases. Displacement onto immediate tactical objective begins. Flirtation rises.
3. **Sustained pressure (mission complications, intimate disclosure required, paternal authority present):** Sexualization, undoing, geographic-cure planning. Drinking starts or increases. Meta-narration ("classic me") intensifies.
4. **High load (decisions with no good options; intimate partner reaching past the costume; grief-adjacent stimulus):** Tier III emerges. Splitting on any paternal authority present. Unilateral action attempted. Denial of grief active. Dissociative absenting visible.
5. **Catastrophic load (existential threat to chosen family; unbearable interior pressure with no operational outlet):** Suicide-by-mission risk surfaces. Acting out via combat-seeking. Regression possible if paternal figure present.
6. **Post-crisis:** Performance of recovery in front of others; private acting-out (drinking, sex, or motion); refusal of debrief on affective content; silent stratification of the new loss atop the prior ones.

---

### 8. Summary

The defensive architecture is built for one purpose: **to keep the grief moving so it never settles long enough to crush him.** Humor moves it sideways into deflection. Music moves it backward into a sealed maternal time. Mission moves it forward into objective. Sex moves it outward into other bodies. Alcohol slows the whole system. Motion keeps the room from getting small enough to corner him. Unilateral action keeps him from being the boy whose fate was decided by others. Splitting keeps the father intact as villain rather than as the more devastating mixed object. Dissociation keeps him present-enough without requiring him to *be* present.

The apparatus has worked. He is alive, he is loved, he leads a team that has saved galaxies. The apparatus has also cost him: the intimacies he wants, the sobriety he could have, the self-knowledge he is bright enough to bear but has never been still enough to acquire. The defenses are not the disease; the unmetabolized grief is the disease, and the defenses are the brilliant, exhausting, costly improvisation of a child who had to invent his own survival without instruction.

The clinically relevant fact for any future intervention is this: **none of his primary defenses can be removed without first providing a substitute container for the affect they manage.** Take away the humor, the music, the motion, the drink, the costume — and the grief, undiminished by forty years of carriage, would arrive at full force into a personality that has never once practiced receiving it. He is, for this reason, both more treatable and more fragile than he appears. The cost


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — SUBJECT: PETER JASON QUILL

*Decade-by-decade clinical mapping. Affect regulation, cognitive style, self-concept, defensive architecture, relational template — tracked from the foundational rupture forward, with each stratum derived from cited canon and read against established trauma and developmental frameworks (Bowlby/Main attachment; Herman's tripartite trauma model; Linehan affect-regulation taxonomy; Kernberg on grandiose defenses in non-narcissists; Bromberg on dissociative self-state systems).*

---

## I. PRE-RUPTURE INFANCY AND THE CHILDHOOD STRATUM (~age 0–11, Earth, rural Missouri)

**Baseline data, inferred from Englehart 1976 and consistent flashback material across runs.** Single-mother household, Meredith Quill the sole reliable attachment figure, father absent (and across continuities, willfully so). The pre-rupture period is the only one in Quill's life for which there is evidence of *secure-leaning* attachment: he is depicted in flashback as a normally affectionate child, capable of trust, with a developmental trajectory that does not predict the later pathology. This matters clinically because it establishes that the eventual presentation is **acquired, not constitutional** — the personality structure has a "before."

**Affect regulation, pre-rupture.** Co-regulated through the mother. The audio bond — music played in the home, the seed of the lifelong Earth-pop fixation — is already encoded as a maternal-proximal soothing channel. He is learning, normally, to borrow her nervous system to settle his own. This developmental task is *interrupted mid-process*. He never finishes internalizing the soothing function; the channel remains externalized in audio for the rest of his life.

**Cognitive style, pre-rupture.** Undocumented in detail, but the later capacity for fast pattern-reading, verbal facility, and improvisational humor implies a child with high verbal intelligence and a temperamentally fast nervous system — qualities that, in a stable environment, would have produced a quick and curious adult, and in the actual environment produced a quick and *vigilant* one.

**Self-concept, pre-rupture.** Coherent, undivided. There is one Peter. The split into Peter/Star-Lord has not yet been required.

---

## II. THE RUPTURE AND THE INSTITUTIONAL DECADE (~age 11–early 20s)

**The traumatic event.** The mother is killed by alien assassins sent for *him*. He survives because she stands between him and them. The clinical features of this single event are catastrophic and unusually compounded:

- Witnessed violent death of the sole attachment figure.
- Causal implication of the self in the death ("they came for me").
- Perpetrators non-human, unfamiliar, unprocessable within the available childhood schema — there is no available narrative ("a bad man hurt mama") that contains what he saw.
- No surviving second attachment figure to provide post-trauma co-regulation.
- The cosmic/alien dimension of the trauma is *socially unsharable* — no foster placement, no counselor, no peer will believe him; the trauma becomes secret as well as severe.

Per Herman's framework this is not single-incident PTSD substrate; it is the seed of complex PTSD, because the post-event environment (foster bouncing, institutional handlers, no consistent caregiver) re-traumatizes through abandonment-coded experience for years afterward.

**Affect regulation in the institutional years.** Collapses into externalization. Englehart's depiction is explicit: surly, hostile, fighting authority, friendless. This is the classic post-traumatic child presentation — affect is unmodulated because the modulating relationship is gone, and is discharged as aggression because aggression keeps adults at a distance, which is functionally protective (adults proved lethal-adjacent). He is not "bad"; he is **defending against re-attachment to anyone who could be taken**.

**Cognitive style.** Constricts to immediate threat-survey. Long-horizon planning offline; tactical survival online. He learns to read rooms (which foster adult is dangerous, which is merely indifferent, which can be manipulated) and to read exits. This skill set is preserved verbatim into adult Quill — the captain who reads a Knowhere bar in three seconds is the boy who read a group home in three.

**Self-concept.** Begins to split. The "Peter who could not save her" is intolerable and is encysted; a more functional surface-self is grown over it. The eventual Star-Lord persona is not yet built, but the foundation — *the need for a self other than the one in the memory* — is laid in this decade.

**Defensive architecture, end of period.** Reaction-formation against helplessness via stolen agency (the NASA-adjacent theft, the literal climbing-into-a-spaceship). The escape from Earth is not mere wanderlust; it is a **geographic re-enactment**, this time chosen — *I will be the one who leaves before I am the one who is left.* This becomes a lifelong template.

---

## III. THE COSMIC APPRENTICESHIP AND THE EARLY MASK (~early 20s–early 30s; original Englehart-through-Starlin era)

The Master of the Sun confers the Star-Lord vocation. Clinically, the importance is not the title but **the timing**: an unmoored young man with no internal compass is handed a stranger's mission and accepts it because he has none of his own. This is identity-by-conscription, and it is the first iteration of a pattern that will repeat — accept the grand role, then discover it does not fit, then flee.

**Affect regulation, this stratum.** Improving on the institutional-decade baseline because *motion itself is regulatory*. Space gives him what foster care could not: legitimate, continuous, structured movement. The hypervigilance that was maladaptive in a Missouri group home is adaptive in vacuum. He is, briefly, *competent for his nervous system*. This is the first period in which the persona begins to feel like a fit rather than a costume — and this is also why he will keep returning to it.

**Cognitive style.** Begins the lifelong asymmetry: **excellent tactical, weak strategic.** He performs well in discrete missions and poorly in long-arc statecraft. The reason is developmental: tactical thinking is what survived the rupture; strategic thinking is what would have required a stable adult modeling future-horizon planning, which he did not have.

**Self-concept.** First stabilization of the persona. "Star-Lord" begins to do real work: it externalizes the function the lost mother used to perform — *it tells him who he is*. The fact that the name is **announced rather than earned** (he introduces himself with it; the cosmos does not) is the clinical tell that this is a self-prescription, not a recognition.

**Defenses present, this stratum.** Humor is operational but not yet central. The signature glibness comes later, as accumulated loss raises the regulatory demand. In this period he is still capable of relatively direct sincerity, which is why earliest Englehart-vintage Quill reads as *more sincere and angrier* than later iterations.

---

## IV. THE BLACK-OPS / KREE MILITARY YEARS AND THE CONQUEST CATASTROPHE (~early 30s; pre- and intra-Annihilation: Conquest)

Quill re-emerges as a hardened operative inside Kree military command. The clinical significance: he has migrated from solo cosmic-vocation to **institutional embed**, which is the adult version of the foster-care container — a structure that holds him while requiring no intimacy. He is functional here precisely because the relational stakes are low and the mission stakes are high. He has found the environment his post-traumatic nervous system is optimized for.

**The Phalanx mission failure.** He leads; teammates die; he is imprisoned. This is the **second formative wound**, and structurally it is the inverse of the first: in the first, he was a child who could not save the adult who tried to save him; in this, he is the adult who could not save the subordinates who trusted his command. The reactivation is exact. The guilt of the first trauma — *they died because of me* — is reinscribed with adult agency this time, which makes it harder to defend against.

**Affect regulation, post-Conquest.** Begins the substance-use slope in earnest. Drinking moves from social to regulatory. The prison interval (Kyln) provides forced stillness, which is the worst available environment for him; he emerges *more* defended, not less.

**Cognitive style, post-Conquest.** The strategic deficit becomes visible to him for the first time. He knows, after Conquest, that he loses at the second-order level. Rather than rebuild the deficient capacity, he **doubles down on tactical** and recruits around the weakness — the future Guardians will include strategic and analytical minds (Gamora's threat-modeling, Rocket's engineering forecasting) whose function is to *compensate for his cognitive shape without him having to name the compensation*.

**Self-concept, post-Conquest.** First explicit fracture in the Star-Lord identity. The persona has now failed in the field; he cannot fully believe in it anymore. But he cannot abandon it either, because what is underneath — the boy who could not save his mother, now also the commander who could not save his team — is unlivable. So he keeps the costume and adds a layer of *ironic distance from it*. From this point forward Quill will mock the name "Star-Lord" *as he uses it*. The mockery is the new load-bearing piece — it lets him keep the structure while pre-disclaiming it.

**Defensive architecture, end of period.** Humor moves to primary. This is the clinical inflection point at which Quill becomes the *talker* he is for the rest of canon.

---

## V. THE GUARDIANS FOUNDER ERA AND THE MANTIS REVELATION (~early-to-mid 30s; Abnett & Lanning, 2008–2010)

He builds the team as a *preventive* force — explicitly framed as stopping the next catastrophe before it begins. The motivational structure is transparent under analysis: he is constructing the apparatus that would have saved his mother. The Guardians are reparative fantasy made operational.

**Affect regulation, this stratum.** Externalized through the team itself. The Guardians do for adult Quill what Meredith did for child Quill — they are an environment that metabolizes his affect for him. He laughs because Rocket is a foil; he is reckless because Drax will catch the shrapnel; he can be a leader because Gamora corrects his strategy without humiliating him. He has, for the first time since age 11, **a co-regulating system**. This is also why he cannot risk losing them and why he will, predictably, do the thing that risks losing them.

**The Mantis mind-wipe.** Under pressure to assemble the team, he has Mantis telepathically erase their memory of consenting to the founding. Clinically this is the most diagnostic single act in the entire dossier. It is not characterological cruelty; it is **omnipotent control as defense against helplessness** (Winnicott; Kernberg) — the child who could not control the assassins' arrival becomes the adult who will not allow others' free agreement to determine whether his protective structure exists. He cannot tolerate the possibility of *no*. So he forecloses the question.

The revelation fractures the team. He absorbs the consequence and does not, fully, learn from it — the unilateral-deception reflex recurs in every subsequent run. It is not a mistake; it is a **structural feature** of how he handles existential relational stakes.

**Cognitive style.** Best of his life, in terms of read-the-room and rally-the-room. The strategic deficit is concealed by team composition. He looks, in this period, like a competent captain because he has staffed around his own holes.

**Self-concept.** Briefly coherent. Star-Lord fits because the Guardians validate it. This is the longest period of self-cohesion in his adult life, and it ends with the Mantis blowback, which proves to him that the cohesion was rented, not owned.

**Cancerverse / Thanos Imperative.** Self-sacrificial pinning of Thanos with Nova. This is the first frank suicide-by-mission. It is *successful* — he survives by writerly grace, not by intent. Clinically, the willingness to die-for-the-mission is by this point a **stable feature of his stress response at the catastrophic ceiling**. The mother-death template completes itself: *I will be the one who stands between them and the thing that is coming.*

The unexplained return introduces a new permanent dynamic: he has now died, and reality has refused to keep him dead. He carries the metaphysical insult of being **un-buryable** — every subsequent loss is shadowed by the suspicion that he is the wrong one to keep surviving.

---

## VI. THE BENDIS DECADE — CHARISMATIC ROGUE, PATERNAL CONFRONTATION (~mid-to-late 30s; Bendis vol. 3, 2013–2015)

Reframed as wisecracking rogue with daddy issues centered on J'son of Spartax. The reframe is consistent with prior psychological data; it foregrounds material that was always there.

**Affect regulation, this stratum.** Increasingly dependent on **performance**. The glibness is now a constant signal carrier — it runs in the background even when no one is watching. Music, sex, drink. The Kitty Pryde proposal-by-hologram is a near-perfect somatic-relational artifact: he proposes marriage *while remaining physically off-planet*. The intimacy is real; the body is absent. This is the attachment double-bind made literal — *I want you and I cannot be in the room with you*.

**Cognitive style.** Verbal acuity at lifetime peak. Strategic deficit unchanged. He is elected/declared President of Spartax and **flees the daily administrative work of the role**. The pattern is now diagnostic: he can *acquire* any position; he cannot *occupy* it. This is not laziness; it is that any role with calendar-time, recurring meetings, and predictable obligations replicates the conditions that allowed his mother to be found at home and killed. **Stillness is unsafe.** Presidency requires stillness. He flees.

**Self-concept, this stratum.** The Peter/Star-Lord split is at its most visible. Bendis writes scenes in which Quill — usually after sex, usually slightly drunk — drops the persona briefly and is unbearable to himself in the silence, then re-armors before the partner notices. The split is not pathological in the dissociative-disorder sense; it is **dissociative-spectrum self-state oscillation** (Bromberg) — he has multiple self-states that are mutually aware but separately operative, and the transitions are conscious but not freely chosen.

**Father-coded authority.** J'son catalyzes the lifetime pattern of **splitting under paternal pressure** — idealize, demand, reject. He cannot make peace with the father because the father is structurally a placeholder for the unanswerable question *where were you when she died*. No actual J'son could answer it. So no actual J'son will be enough.

**Romantic ledger.** Short cycles, warm contact, withdrawal, image-management of the withdrawal. He persuades partners to forgive his absences using the same verbal apparatus he uses on enemies — and this is, eventually, what Kitty Pryde correctly refuses to keep accepting.

---

## VII. THE DUGGAN / EWING TRANSITIONAL PERIOD (~late 30s/early 40s subjective; post-Bendis runs)

Lower-profile psychologically; period of **accumulated wear without new catastrophe**. The Guardians configurations shift; he loses and regains the captaincy; the glibness becomes habitual rather than performative — the costume now wears itself. Drinking becomes more solitary and less narratively foregrounded; the absence of foregrounding is itself a clinical signal (it is no longer remarkable to the people around him).

**Affect regulation.** Flattens. Less peak hilarity, less peak despair. The system is running on reduced amplitude — a chronic-trauma adaptation in which the cost of large affect has become prohibitive and the cost of no affect is preferable.

**Cognitive style.** Slight deterioration in tactical sharpness consistent with prolonged subclinical alcohol use and untreated trauma load. Still functional; no longer brilliant.

**Self-concept.** Quietly eroding. He has been Star-Lord long enough that the persona has lost some of its restitutive charge; it no longer pays back the debt to the ghost as well as it used to. Restitution requires *novel* heroism; routine heroism just keeps the ledger from getting worse.

---

## VIII. THE CATES EXILE AND THE STACKED-GRIEF STRATUM (subjective centuries; chronological months)

The Pleasure Garden / pocket-dimension exile. He marries, raises children, ages alongside them, **loses them**, returns. The clinical consequences are unique in his life history and arguably unique in his published cohort.

- **Acute compounded bereavement.** A full mortal life's worth of loved-and-lost in subjective time, returned to a context where none of those losses are socially witnessed.
- **Identity disjunction.** The Peter who returns is decades older internally than the Star-Lord persona was built to contain. The persona, sized for a man in his 30s, now hangs on a man who has *interiorly* lived a full lifespan.
- **Survivor guilt, third iteration.** First the mother. Then the Phalanx team. Now a wife and children whose existence cannot be verified outside his own head.
- **The unsharability problem at maximum.** Even other Guardians cannot witness this grief, because for them it did not happen on a witnessable timescale.

**Affect regulation, post-exile.** Marked shift. Drinking moves from social-with-solitary-episodes to **solitary-with-social-episodes**. Glibness is still deployed but at lower frequency and with visible fatigue; teammates notice. He is described and shown as *quieter*. This is not improvement. This is the regulatory system finally running out of energy for the show.

**Cognitive style, post-exile.** First evidence of *long-horizon thinking* — paradoxically. Having lived an entire interior life of children growing up, he understands time differently. He is, for the first time, capable of thinking in decades. But he uses this capacity mostly for grief, not planning. The strategic deficit on outer-life decisions persists; the long-horizon capacity has been routed inward, into mourning.

**Self-concept, post-exile.** The Peter/Star-Lord split is now joined by a **third self-state**: the husband-father he was in the Garden. This third self is the only one of the three that was ever fully relationally embedded, and it is the one no one in the current world can see. He guards it because it is the only intact attachment experience of his life *and* it is gone. Naming it would dissolve it. So he does not name it.

**Defensive architecture, post-exile.** Humor demoted from primary to secondary for the first time since the Conquest catastrophe. Primary defense is now **selective silence** — refusal to discuss the exile, refusal to discuss the Cancerverse, refusal to discuss the boy in Missouri. Silence is cheaper than performance and, at this point in his life, all he can afford.

---

## IX. CROSS-STRATUM SYNTHESIS — WHAT EVOLVED, WHAT DID NOT, WHAT ACCRUED

**What evolved.**
- **Defenses upgraded in sophistication**: aggression (institutional decade) → vocation-acceptance (apprenticeship) → humor (post-Conquest) → omnipotent-control deception (founder era) → performative persona-with-irony (Bendis) → selective silence (post-exile). Each upgrade preserves function while reducing visibility — he has become harder to read, not healthier.
- **Time-horizon for grief**: lengthened, post-exile, from acute-suppressed to chronic-acknowledged-but-unspoken.
- **Self-state count**: increased from two (Peter/Star-Lord) to three (Peter/Star-Lord/Garden-husband).
- **Regulatory amplitude**: decreased. He runs on a smaller dynamic range than he used to.

**What did not evolve.**
- **Core attachment template.** Disorganized-leaning insecure across every decade. No corrective relational experience has been allowed to stabilize. The Garden marriage came closest and was annihilated, which functions as confirmation rather than correction.
- **Strategic-thinking deficit on outer-life decisions.** Compensated by team composition, never repaired.
- **Unilateral-decision reflex under existential relational stakes.** Mantis, Spartax, the Cancerverse — same reflex, three contexts, three decades.
- **Father-coded splitting.** Active whenever a paternal figure appears. Not modulated.
- **The mother-loss as the load-bearing referent.** Every defense ultimately answers to it.

**What accrued.**
- **Loss ledger**: mother → Phalanx team → Cancerverse interval → various teammates across runs → Garden family → portions of his own usable past (the Cancerverse contamination, the exile time). The ledger is monotonic; nothing has been subtracted.
- **Substance load.** Increasing baseline, decreasing peak — the curve of a moderate AUD on a long timeline without intervention.
- **Unwitnessed interior life.** Grows with every exile, every death-and-return, every refusal to speak. By the post-Cates stratum the interior is substantially larger than the exterior, and the exterior is starting to feel, to him, like the smaller of the two rooms he lives in.

**The longitudinal conclusion.** Quill's psychological development is not a curve; it is a **stratigraphy**. Nothing healed; everything layered. The earliest wound is still the bottom stratum and still bears the weight of every layer above it. The Star-Lord persona — load-bearing in stratum III, optimal in stratum V, frayed in stratum VI, fatigued in stratum VII, hollowed in stratum VIII — has done its job for thirty subjective years and several hundred more in exile. It is now visibly tired in canon, and the man under it is visibly older than the costume can disguise.

He is, clinically, exactly where the framework predicts a complex-PTSD subject with stacked unprocessed grief and untreated AUD would be after this many decades of motion-as-treatment: **functional, beloved, structurally unchanged, and quietly running out of the energy that ran him**. The interventions that would help him are the ones he has organized his entire life to make impossible — stillness, sustained witnessed disclosure, sobriety long enough to feel what sobriety reveals. None are likely to occur unaided. All remain, in principle, available.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: PETER JASON QUILL

**File §4 | Compiled UATU | Cross-referenced against §1 (History), §2 (Medical), §3 (Psychological)**

---

## 4.0 Framing Note on Method

The subject has never been formally evaluated. No clinician of record. No intake, no MMPI, no structured interview, no longitudinal chart. What follows is a behavioral-evidence diagnostic synthesis built from approximately five decades of published canon (1976–present), cross-validated against repeated observers (Drax, Gamora, Rocket, Mantis, Nova/Richard Rider, Kitty Pryde, Nikki, Yondu in mentor-coded interactions, J'son in adversarial-paternal interactions). The standard applied is *converging behavioral evidence across multiple writers, multiple decades, and multiple stress contexts.* A pattern that appears once in one run is noted as suggestive; a pattern that appears in Englehart, Abnett & Lanning, Bendis, AND Cates is treated as structural.

Diagnostic frameworks invoked are DSM-5-TR and ICD-11, with the latter preferred for trauma-spectrum work (the ICD-11 C-PTSD construct fits the subject better than any DSM-5-TR analog). Where Terran nosology is structurally inadequate to a xenobiological hybrid with multi-century subjective time exposure, this is flagged rather than papered over.

---

## 4.1 PRIMARY DIAGNOSIS — Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41)

**Confidence: very high.** This is the load-bearing diagnosis. All other findings either feed into it, derive from it, or sit comorbidly beside it.

### 4.1.1 Etiology

The trauma exposure required by ICD-11 6B41 is "exposure to an event or series of events of an extremely threatening or horrific nature, most commonly prolonged or repetitive events from which escape is difficult or impossible." The subject meets this threshold on multiple, layered axes:

- **Index trauma (childhood, single-event-with-prolonged-sequelae):** Witnessing of maternal death by alien assassins, contextualized by the subject's own causal centrality (they came for him; she died interposing). This single event satisfies criterion A on its own. It is also developmentally catastrophic — it occurred in latency or pre-adolescence, before the subject possessed cognitive or social resources to metabolize it, and was followed not by stabilizing caregiving but by abduction or institutional placement (variant by continuity; in all canons the post-event environment is *non-restorative*).

- **Childhood prolonged trauma:** Per Englehart's foundational telling and consistent with all later expansions, the subject moves through foster placements, group homes, or off-world handlers in a chronic state of unwanted-ness. No depicted secure attachment figure between Meredith and (variably) Yondu's Ravagers, who do not constitute a corrective relationship — they constitute a continuation of conditional belonging under threat.

- **Adult prolonged trauma:** Annihilation, the Phalanx campaign (Conquest), the Cancerverse incursion, War of Kings, Infinity, the Cates-era pocket-dimension exile. The subject has spent his published adulthood inside an unbroken sequence of combat and bereavement. There is no peacetime baseline in this file.

- **Subjective-time trauma without witnesses:** The Cates exile is its own etiologic stratum. The subject lived a full mortal life — partnered, parented, aged, lost — inside a duration nobody around him shared. This is bereavement *without communal recognition*, which the grief literature identifies as the highest-risk substrate for prolonged grief and for trauma sequelae.

### 4.1.2 Symptom mapping (ICD-11 6B41 criteria)

ICD-11 C-PTSD requires the three PTSD core clusters PLUS three "disturbances in self-organization" (DSO) clusters. Each is satisfied.

**Core 1 — Re-experiencing in the here and now:**
- Recurrent recourse to Terran pop-cultural artifacts of the period immediately preceding the index trauma. The mixtape/Walkman/cassette/Zune attachment (canonized in cinematic, paralleled in print via persistent 70s/80s music references and Earth-nostalgia beats) is not hobby; it is *sensory re-immersion in the pre-trauma sensorium*. Classic intrusive-memory management dressed as taste.
- Documented startle and dissociation in moments of acoustic or olfactory match. Rocket has observed the subject "go somewhere else" mid-conversation; Gamora has noted unprompted silences after specific triggers (children, mothers, Earth-coded imagery).
- Refusal to narrate the Cancerverse and refusal to narrate the Pleasure-Garden exile — when pressed, the subject either jokes, leaves the room, or pours another drink. This is avoidance of intrusive re-experiencing, not absence of it.

**Core 2 — Avoidance:**
- Geographic: he lives on a ship. The vessel is a mobile avoidance apparatus.
- Relational: serial short-arc romance; refusal of the Spartax throne; refusal of all bureaucratic permanence.
- Conversational: documented topic-changes around mother, exile, Cancerverse. Substitutes humor for content with high reliability — the deflection rate approaches 1.0 in the high-affect register.

**Core 3 — Persistent sense of current threat:**
- Sleeps armed or near weapons. Element gun within reach during downtime per multiple panels across runs.
- Hyperscan of unfamiliar rooms; pattern observable in bar entries and diplomatic settings alike.
- Exaggerated startle to abrupt arrivals; over-quick draw in low-threat scenarios (commented on by teammates).

**DSO 1 — Affect dysregulation:**
- Affect-regulating substance use (see §4.2).
- Anger flashes disproportionate to provocation, particularly toward father-coded figures and toward allies who deceive him.
- Sexual behavior as state-regulator rather than relational expression.

**DSO 2 — Negative self-concept:**
- Self-deprecating humor that, under cross-examination by intimates, is *believed*. The subject's jokes about himself — incompetence, fraudulence, the absurdity of the "Star-Lord" name — are not pure deflection; they are partial confessions. When alone with Gamora or in confessional beats with Rocket, the joke-mask thins and the underlying self-assessment is genuinely poor.
- Survivor-guilt structure: he organizes his life around being worth the cost of his mother's death, which is to say, he begins from the axiom that he is not.

**DSO 3 — Disturbances in relationships:**
- Inability to sustain calendar-time intimacy despite high capacity for crisis-time intimacy. The Kitty Pryde proposal-by-hologram is paradigmatic: maximum gesture, minimum proximity.
- Recurrent unilateral decisions affecting allies (Mantis mind-wipe; tactical secrecy patterns) — the relational disturbance is not coldness, it is *control as substitute for trust*.

### 4.1.3 Course over time

The C-PTSD presentation has *worsened in severity while improving in surface presentation*. Across publication chronology:

- **Englehart-era (latency-period coded):** Raw, hostile, friendless, openly embittered. The wound is on the outside.
- **Cosmic-operative middle period (post-Annihilation):** Hardened, compartmentalized, command-functional, guilt-bearing. The wound has been *encrypted into competence*.
- **Abnett & Lanning founder era:** Charisma re-emerges; the persona stabilizes as a public-facing apparatus. The Mantis incident reveals the underlying control structure is intact and operative.
- **Bendis era:** Maximum performative function, maximum mask polish, maximum intimacy-avoidance dressed as roguishness. The mask works best; the man is most absent.
- **Cates and after:** The mask cracks visibly. Solitary drinking increases. The performance is recognizably tired to observers. He is quieter, slower to joke, slower to deflect. Paradoxically this is *progress in symptom visibility, regression in symptom severity*. The wound is reasserting itself against an exhausted defense structure.

This is the classic mid-life decompensation pattern in untreated C-PTSD: the defenses that carried the subject through early adulthood metabolize less efficiently as new losses accrete, and the subject becomes more recognizably symptomatic to outside observers even as he continues to function.

---

## 4.2 COMORBID — Alcohol Use Disorder, Moderate, Progressive (DSM-5-TR 303.90 / ICD-11 6C40.2)

**Confidence: high.**

### 4.2.1 Criterion mapping

Of the eleven DSM-5-TR criteria, the subject meets — by behavioral evidence across runs — approximately six to seven, placing him in the *moderate* severity band (4–5 = moderate; 6+ = severe; he is on the cusp).

- **Larger amounts / longer than intended:** Consistent in bar scenes from Abnett-Lanning onward; lateness following overnight drinking sessions is documented across Bendis.
- **Persistent desire or unsuccessful efforts to cut down:** Not directly canonized; inferred from intermittent dry stretches followed by relapse pattern.
- **Time spent obtaining/using/recovering:** The subject's downtime is structurally organized around drinking environments (cantinas, the ship's stores, social settings selected for availability).
- **Craving:** Not directly canonized.
- **Failure to fulfill obligations:** Chronic lateness, missed rendezvous, missed romantic commitments. Pattern attested by Kitty Pryde and by multiple Guardians-era teammates.
- **Continued use despite social/interpersonal problems:** Yes; teammates have explicitly objected, no sustained behavior change.
- **Activities given up:** Less attested.
- **Use in physically hazardous situations:** Yes; piloting and combat decisions while impaired have been depicted or strongly implied.
- **Continued use despite physical/psychological problems:** Yes; the subject knows the drinking is grief-management and continues anyway.
- **Tolerance:** Apparent; baseline consumption that would impair a baseline human appears subjectively manageable to him, partly Spartoi physiology, partly tolerance.
- **Withdrawal:** Not depicted; possibly masked by hybrid physiology.

### 4.2.2 Function

This is *use as affect regulator*, not use as recreation. The drinking does work the subject cannot do otherwise: it bridges the gap between the persona and the man, anesthetizes the intrusive material C-PTSD generates in unstructured time, and provides a socially-acceptable explanation for emotional unavailability ("just hungover") that the real explanation (unmetabolized maternal bereavement, layered combat trauma, century-scale grief from the exile) would not survive without rupturing the persona.

### 4.2.3 Trajectory

Moderate and progressing. The Cates-era solitary drinking is the prognostic worry. Social drinking under observation is a different beast from solitary drinking in private quarters; the shift from the former to the latter is the standard inflection point at which moderate AUD becomes severe AUD. The subject is at that inflection.

---

## 4.3 COMORBID — Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89; ICD-11 6B42)

**Confidence: moderate-to-high.**

### 4.3.1 Etiology

Three separable bereavements, none worked through:

1. **Meredith Quill (mother).** The foundational loss. Never funerally processed by the subject; never narratively closed. The grief has been *outrun*, not metabolized.
2. **The Pleasure-Garden family (Cates exile).** A spouse and children lived, aged, and were lost across subjective decades or centuries. The subject returned to mainline reality bearing this and refuses to discuss it. Disenfranchised grief in the technical sense — nobody around him knows the dead, nobody can mourn with him.
3. **Cumulative team losses.** Phalanx-campaign teammates (Conquest); various Guardians across runs; Nova/Richard Rider (the Cancerverse partner). The subject has buried more chosen kin than most field officers.

### 4.3.2 Symptom presentation

PGD requires persistent yearning/longing or preoccupation with the deceased, plus accessory symptoms (identity disruption, disbelief, avoidance of reminders, intense emotional pain, difficulty reintegrating, emotional numbness, sense of meaninglessness, intense loneliness). The subject presents:

- Persistent identity disruption keyed to maternal loss (the entire Peter/Star-Lord split is identity disruption around bereavement).
- Avoidance of reminders specific to the Pleasure-Garden family (he will not name them aloud).
- Intense loneliness obscured by sociability — the subject is rarely literally alone yet reads as relationally isolated to observers.
- Sense of meaninglessness managed by mission-acquisition: each new cosmic crisis is a meaning-prosthetic.

### 4.3.3 Differentiation from C-PTSD

PGD and C-PTSD overlap and are formally separable. The trauma-cluster symptoms (re-experiencing, threat, avoidance) belong to C-PTSD; the bereavement-specific symptoms (yearning, identity disruption keyed to specific dead persons, meaning-loss) belong to PGD. The subject carries both. Treatment would need to address both, sequentially or in parallel, because grief-work that ignores trauma-load destabilizes, and trauma-work that ignores grief-load fails to consolidate.

---

## 4.4 SUBCLINICAL / TRAIT-LEVEL — Narcissistic and Histrionic Defenses Without the Disorders

**Confidence: high that defenses are present; high that disorders are absent.**

The surface presentation invites both diagnoses. The structural evidence refutes both. This distinction matters because the treatment implications diverge radically: a narcissist and a non-narcissist with narcissistic defenses respond to clinical contact in opposite ways.

### 4.4.1 Narcissistic features that are present

- Grandiose self-naming (announces "Star-Lord" unprompted).
- Attention-seeking entrance pattern.
- Sexual conquest as self-state regulation.
- Episodic devaluation of authority figures.
- Difficulty tolerating subordinate status under certain father-coded figures.

### 4.4.2 Why this is not Narcissistic Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.81)

Three structural disqualifiers:

1. **Empathic capacity is intact and operative.** The subject reads teammates accurately, registers their distress as distress (not as resource), and modifies behavior in response. NPD requires a *structural* incapacity to apprehend others as full subjects; the subject demonstrates the opposite, repeatedly, including in moments where it costs him.

2. **The grandiosity is ego-dystonic.** True NPD grandiosity is ego-syntonic — the narcissist *is* the grandiose self and experiences the grandiosity as accurate self-perception. The subject knows the "Star-Lord" persona is a costume. He knows because he can be made to take it off (by intimates, by grief, by his real name spoken at the right moment, by sufficient alcohol). A narcissist cannot.

3. **He accepts subordinate roles without collapse.** Under Nova's command, under Drax's lead in specific tactical situations, in Avengers-team contexts where he is junior — the subject defers without narcissistic injury. NPD cannot do this stably.

The accurate formulation is *narcissistic defense in a non-narcissistic personality structure* — the grandiosity is a load-bearing prosthetic for a wound, not the shape of the self.

### 4.4.3 Histrionic features that are present

- Theatricality of affect.
- Use of physical appearance to engage attention.
- Rapid shifts of expressed emotion.
- Suggestible to atmospheric/musical cues.

### 4.4.4 Why this is not Histrionic Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.50)

The histrionic features serve trauma defense (audience as mirror to confirm the persona is holding); they do not constitute the subject's primary mode of relating. He is fully capable of sustained, non-performative interaction in low-threat dyads (documented with Gamora, with Rocket in late-night ship-deck scenes, with Yondu in mentor moments). HPD requires the theatricality to be the default mode across contexts; the subject has an off-stage register.

---

## 4.5 RIGOROUS DIFFERENTIAL — What He Is Not, and Why

This section explicitly excludes diagnoses a less careful evaluator might assign. Each is named, considered, and ruled out with reasoning.

### 4.5.1 Antisocial Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.7) — RULED OUT

Surface biography (theft, smuggling, killing, evasion of authority) suggests ASPD. The structure refutes it on every axis:

- **Remorse is present and behaviorally operative.** The subject carries the Conquest mission failure as guilt, not as inconvenience. He grieves the dead. ASPD requires absent or shallow remorse.
- **Loyalty to non-instrumental relationships.** ASPD relationships are use-value relationships. The subject's primary relationships are explicitly non-instrumental — he loses material advantage by staying loyal to teammates.
- **Ethical floor.** There are lines he will not cross drunk, broke, cornered, or grieving. ASPD has no such structural floor — only situational caution.
- **Capacity for sustained guilt.** The subject is morally wounded by his own failures of integrity (Mantis incident is remembered and regretted, not rationalized away).

### 4.5.2 Bipolar I / Bipolar II (DSM-5-TR 296.xx) — RULED OUT

The performative high-energy presentation can mimic hypomania. It is not.

- **No autonomous episodes.** The energy is contextual (audience-present, mission-active, intoxicated). It does not arise from endogenous mood machinery.
- **No reduced need for sleep in an episode-defining sense.** Disrupted sleep is trauma-architectural, not mood-architectural.
- **No depressive episodes meeting duration and severity.** Low periods are reactive, brief, and grief-coded.
- **Persona is stable across observation.** Bipolar mood states are *qualitatively different* from the patient's baseline. The subject's "high" is his baseline persona; there is no qualitative shift, only volume control.

### 4.5.3 Major Depressive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 296.2x/3x) — RULED OUT as primary; subthreshold features present

- Low mood when present is reactive and trauma/grief-keyed, not autonomous.
- Anhedonia, when observable, is grief-anhedonia (he can still take pleasure in non-grief-adjacent activities) not melancholic anhedonia (which is pervasive).
- No sustained two-week episode meeting full criteria has been depicted.
- The depressive *features* he does carry are better accounted for by C-PTSD's negative self-concept cluster and by PGD.

### 4.5.4 Generalized Anxiety Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.02) — RULED OUT

Hyperarousal is trauma-keyed (current-threat C-PTSD cluster), not free-floating worry. He does not catastrophize about non-trauma-related futures. He catastrophizes about loss because he has lost.

### 4.5.5 Panic Disorder — RULED OUT

No depicted panic attacks meeting criteria. Stress response is hypervigilant and dissociative-flavored, not panic-spectrum.

### 4.5.6 Substance/Sex Addiction (as primary disorders) — RULED OUT

Both behaviors are *symptomatic of C-PTSD's affect dysregulation cluster* rather than primary processes. Treating either as the primary problem would miss the mechanism. (AUD is diagnosed comorbidly above because it has progressed to disorder-level on its own criteria, but its etiology is downstream of the trauma.)

### 4.5.7 Borderline Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.83) — CAREFULLY RULED OUT

This is the differential most worth taking seriously and the easiest to get wrong. C-PTSD and BPD overlap substantially in surface presentation (affect dysregulation, relationship instability, identity disturbance). The DSM-5-TR/ICD-11 differentiation rests on:

- **Identity disturbance pattern.** BPD identity is *unstable across time* — the patient does not know who they are from week to week. The subject has a stable persona across decades; his disturbance is *bifurcated* (Peter vs. Star-Lord), not protean.
- **Idealization/devaluation pattern.** BPD splits intimate partners constantly. The subject splits *father-figures* (a trauma-specific pattern), not partners or teammates generally. His teammate relationships are remarkably stable affectively.
- **Abandonment terror.** Present in the subject but *enacted as preemptive withdrawal* rather than as the frantic-clinging-plus-rage cycle characteristic of BPD.
- **Self-harm and suicidality.** BPD presents with parasuicidal gesture patterns. The subject's self-sacrificial behavior is *mission-coded* and morally-framed (Cancerverse choice), not parasuicidal gesture. This is, however, the closest the subject comes to BPD territory and is worth monitoring.

The accurate read is that the subject has *trauma-spectrum relational disturbance* (DSO cluster of C-PTSD), not BPD. The distinction is etiologic and prognostic — C-PTSD with grief-overlay has better long-term prognosis with appropriate treatment than BPD does.

### 4.5.8 Dissociative Identity Disorder — RULED OUT

The Peter/Star-Lord split is a *persona/self bifurcation* under unified executive control, not dissociated alters with amnesic barriers. The subject knows he is doing the persona. There is no amnesia between states.

### 4.5.9 Schizoid or Schizotypal — RULED OUT

The subject is structurally relationally hungry, not relationally indifferent. His isolation is avoidant-defensive, not constitutional.

### 4.5.10 Autism-Spectrum (low support need) — RULED OUT

Social fluency is high; reading rooms is a core competence; affective attunement to others is intact. Sensory profile is unremarkable except as trauma-keyed.

---

## 4.6 XENOBIOLOGICAL AND SUBJECTIVE-TIME CAVEATS

Three considerations stand outside Terran nosology and must be flagged.

1. **Spartoi hybrid neurochemistry.** Baseline neurotransmitter assumptions underlying D


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: PETER JASON QUILL

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across published canon (Englehart 1976 → present). Tells indexed by condition-state, then by channel (somatic, verbal, kinetic, ritual, decisional). Where the same tell recurs across writers and decades, flagged HIGH CONFIDENCE. Where inferred from convergent indirect evidence, flagged DERIVED.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM (rare; usually transitional)

True calm in Subject is a narrow band — observable mostly in the small hours aboard the *Milano* (and successor vessels) when crew are asleep, or during planetfall on uninhabited worlds with no mission timer.

**Somatic baseline.** Posture loosens by roughly the angle of his shoulders; the half-cocked left shoulder he carries in company drops to level. Weight transfers off the balls of the feet onto the heels. Element gun is set down within arm's reach but not on his person. He uncrosses the dominant-hand thumb from the holster strap (a touch-tell almost always present otherwise).

**Verbal.** Sentence length increases. The reflexive joke-tax on every utterance drops from approximately one quip per three lines to one per ten. He uses people's full given names instead of nicknames ("Gamora" instead of "Gam"). Voice drops a quarter-octave; cadence slows.

**Kinetic / ritual.** Music selection skews to slower tracks — ballads, melancholic pop, mid-tempo rock — rather than the up-tempo curation he uses as social armor. He will sit with one boot off, one boot on, an oddly consistent half-shed posture that suggests neither full rest nor full readiness. Drinks one drink, slowly. Cleans the element gun by hand rather than by maintenance protocol — turning it over, sighting along the barrel as a sensory grounding gesture more than maintenance.

**Decisional.** Will make long-horizon decisions only here — repair schedules, route planning, replenishment runs. The strategically weak Quill of crisis is replaced briefly by a competent quartermaster. Anything decided in calm tends to survive; anything decided in stress tends to be re-litigated. Operational note: the highest-leverage point of approach for negotiation with him is the hour after he has finished a meal and before he has finished his second drink.

---

## II. LOW-GRADE SOCIAL OPERATION (default presentation)

This is the Subject's longest-running daily state — bridge banter, port bars, market negotiations, team meetings.

**Somatic.** Right hand free, left hand near holster or belt. Weight on left foot, right foot canted outward roughly fifteen degrees — a duelist's stance disguised as a lounge. He blinks less than baseline human average when speaking, more when listening. Eye-contact pattern: high during his own speech (selling), broken during others' (processing). When listening to something he disagrees with, he looks at the speaker's mouth rather than eyes — a tell he reads as politeness and others read as predation.

**Verbal.** Quip-rate at conversational maximum. Self-deprecation deployed early in any new acquaintance — a preemptive lowering of the bar so that any later failure is already priced in. References to 20th-century Earth media at roughly one per five minutes; these are tested as compatibility checks (does the listener get it? not-getting-it slots them into "outsider," getting-it into "found family candidate"). Name-drops his own alias more than is strictly required ("Star-Lord — y'know, like, *the* Star-Lord") — a recurring micro-tell of the persona's brittleness.

**Kinetic / ritual.** Will enter a new room and clock exits within four seconds — a survival behavior that has become so automatic it reads as casual glancing. Touches objects (bar tops, table edges, console rims) more than necessary; tactile reassurance that the environment is real. With women he is courting, hands move in measured deliberate arcs; with men he is sizing up, hands stay closer to the body.

**Decisional.** Will agree to small things rapidly, large things never. Defers any major commitment with a joke. The rule of thumb: if his first response to a proposal is humor, he is buying time; if his first response is a question about specifics, he is interested; if it is silence followed by a topic change, he has refused without saying so.

---

## III. MILD STRESS / TIME PRESSURE

Mission briefings going sideways, an unexpected bill at port, a teammate annoyed with him, a romantic partner asking a question he does not want to answer.

**Somatic.** Jaw muscle visible at the hinge (left side more than right). Touches the back of his neck with the right hand — the most reliable single tell in the entire file; recurs across every writer who has drawn him with hands on panel. Breathing shallows into upper chest. He will start tonguing the inside of his left cheek between sentences.

**Verbal.** Jokes intensify in frequency but degrade in quality — the wit becomes mechanical, the punchlines arrive slightly off-beat. He begins finishing other people's sentences. Volume creeps up roughly fifteen percent. Begins to interrupt — particularly interrupts women in his life mid-question, the question being the actual stressor.

**Kinetic.** Pacing in tight loops, counterclockwise more often than clockwise (DERIVED from observed cockpit-deck blocking across multiple runs). Will pick up and set down an object — usually the element gun, a flask, or a music device — three or four times in rapid succession without using it. Re-checks gear that was checked five minutes ago.

**Ritual.** Music gets switched to something faster and louder. Drink poured but not finished — abandoned on the console when something pulls him away, and he will not return to that specific glass even if it is still cold.

**Decisional.** Begins to over-promise. Commits to two incompatible courses of action within the same hour to satisfy two different stakeholders. Will not yet lie outright; will omit. Begins running the "I'll handle it" gambit — taking on tasks unilaterally to remove relational negotiation from the situation.

---

## IV. ACUTE THREAT / COMBAT

Where Subject is, paradoxically, most stable. The persona was built for this.

**Somatic.** Pupils dilate; respiratory rate stabilizes (combat-breath training, military residue from Kree period). The neck-touch tell *disappears* entirely — the body has something to do. Posture squares. The duelist's foot-cant becomes a deliberate boxer's stance. Visible reduction in extraneous movement. Pain response blunted; he will fight on broken bones without registering them until after.

**Verbal.** Quip-rate paradoxically rises but the quips become coordinative — he uses them as command-and-control instruments, naming threats by improvised callsigns ("the big guy with the face") that double as targeting instructions to teammates. Voice drops in pitch; gains carrying power. Swearing increases, but in patterned bursts at moments of tactical pivot — a self-cueing mechanism.

**Kinetic.** Movement is improvisational, fluid, asymmetric. Will use element gun for two or three shots, then jet boots, then improvised environmental object, then back to element gun — never the same weapon twice in sequence. Tactical signature: refuses to be predictable, including to his own team. Prefers high ground and exits within line of sight at all times.

**Decisional.** First-order decisions are excellent. Second-order decisions degrade in proportion to time elapsed. He should be the captain of the first fifteen minutes of any engagement and somebody else should be the captain of the next two hours. He does not relinquish command voluntarily.

**Idiosyncratic combat tells.** Talks to the element gun under his breath when reloading or recalibrating — short syllables, not full sentences. Touches the helmet's edge before deploying it, a vestigial gesture from earlier hardware that he has never dropped. Glances upward and to his left during lulls — DERIVED as scanning for incoming, possibly a residual orientation toward where Meredith's killers came from.

---

## V. HIGH STRESS / OVERWHELM (relational complexity exceeding tactical complexity)

The Mantis-mindwipe state. The condition where Subject becomes most dangerous to those who love him.

**Somatic.** Color leaves the face slightly. The neck-touch returns with both hands — palms flat, fingertips at the hairline. He will sit when he should stand, stand when he should sit — postural mismatch with the social register. Sleep degrades; observable next-day puffiness around the eyes.

**Verbal.** Goes quieter than baseline. The jokes drop out almost entirely — and this is the tell. A silent Quill is a Quill making a unilateral decision. He will answer direct questions with single syllables. Begins using formal address ("Captain Pryde," "Agent" instead of nicknames) — distancing language.

**Kinetic.** Disappears from common areas for hours at a time. Goes to engineering, the cargo hold, the cockpit — somewhere defensibly solo. Drinks alone here, not in front of crew.

**Ritual.** Will replay specific tracks on loop — not the curated mixtape, but one song, often a track with maternal coding. Has been observed (Cates run) sitting with the music device in his lap without it playing, just holding it.

**Decisional.** This is the danger zone. Decisions made here are: (a) unilateral, (b) framed as protective of the team, (c) deceptive by omission or commission, (d) regretted within forty-eight hours, (e) defended in public for months afterward to avoid admitting the regret. The Mantis incident is the archetype; the Spartax presidency abandonment is the same mechanism inverted (unilateral *exit* rather than unilateral *commit*).

---

## VI. CATASTROPHIC STRESS / EXTINCTION-LEVEL EVENT

Annihilation, Conquest, Thanos Imperative, Cancerverse, Cates-era cosmic threats.

**Somatic.** Wholly recomposed. The performative looseness vanishes. He becomes still in a way nobody who knows him in low-stakes contexts would recognize. Eye contact becomes direct and held — the only condition under which he does this consistently.

**Verbal.** Speeches. He gives them. Short, declarative, surprisingly unironic. The persona drops because the persona is not equipped for the register — only Peter, the actual man, can speak honestly enough to be believed in extremis. This is when teammates discover, often for the first time in years of association, that he means it.

**Decisional.** Self-sacrificial in trajectory. Will pin the bomb to himself. Will go into the Cancerverse and close the door. Operationally, the rule is: if Quill volunteers for the solo run *and stops joking about it*, he intends not to come back. This is the single highest-priority behavioral flag in the file. Counter-protocol requires removing his agency from the choice — physically extracting him from the deployment surface, not arguing with him.

---

## VII. INTIMACY (sexual)

**Approach.** Initiates with humor, breaks tension with self-deprecation, escalates touch in small testable increments. Reads consent cues precisely — actually attentive, not performatively so. Will retreat at any ambiguity rather than press; this is a real ethical line.

**During.** Reportedly (per the canon scenes that imply it) generous, attentive, communicative in the moment. Not transactional. The persona softens.

**After.** This is the diagnostic moment. Within ninety minutes of intimacy he becomes restless. Will get up for water, for music, for a check on the ship. Reluctant to sleep in the same bed for the full night when the relationship is new; will fall asleep there and wake at oh-three-hundred and relocate. As a relationship matures, this pattern persists but is masked as practical (early shift, ship business). Partners who stay long enough catalog it as withdrawal.

**Verbal post-intimacy.** Cannot do pillow talk that touches on feeling. Can do banter, can do sex talk, cannot do the conversation that begins "where do you see this going." Deflects with a joke calibrated to be charming enough that the partner laughs and lets it go — until the night they don't.

---

## VIII. INTIMACY (non-sexual / chosen-family bonds)

**With Gamora.** Verbal sparring as primary love-language. Physical proximity high; physical contact low — he will stand near her and not touch her, a deliberate respect-distance that is itself intimate. Defers to her tactical judgment more readily than to any other teammate's, including his own.

**With Rocket.** Brother-coded; the bickering is the bond. Stands closer than to anyone else; will physically nudge, lean, prop. Trusts Rocket with mechanical work on his own gear without supervising — a high-trust tell. Will let Rocket insult him in registers he tolerates from nobody else.

**With Drax.** Patience-coded; the only relationship in which Quill is consistently the more emotionally articulate party. Slows his speech, drops idiom, gives Drax space to land jokes. Protective.

**With Groot.** Tender-coded; this is the relationship in which his unmetabolized parental longing finds an acceptable outlet. Voice modulates to a register he uses with no other being.

**With Mantis.** Guilty-coded post the mindwipe incident. Overcorrects with deference. Will not make decisions in her presence without explicitly seeking her input — a behavioral atonement that has outlasted the original injury.

**General chosen-family tell.** He cooks. Across multiple runs, when the team is whole and safe, Quill makes food. This is the only sustained domestic ritual he allows himself. The cooking is mediocre. The act is the point.

---

## IX. GRIEF

**Acute grief (immediate aftermath of loss).** Goes operational. Will not stop moving; will not eat; will not sleep. Jokes intensify into near-mania. This is the most fragile condition under which he presents — and the condition under which he looks most like himself to people who do not know him.

**Acute private grief.** Music. Specifically the older tracks, the ones with the deepest maternal coding. Drinks. Does not weep in any observed canon panel — DERIVED that weeping is reserved for solitude under conditions where no observer will ever record it.

**Sustained grief (the stacked, undischarged kind).** Manifests as the baseline melancholy that has thickened across the runs — slower jokes, longer silences, more drinking, a half-second of delay before responding to his own name. He is, in the Cates-and-after era, *grieving constantly at low amplitude* and concealing it competently from everyone except the reader.

**Grief-anniversary behavior.** DERIVED but high-confidence: he becomes harder to find on dates that correlate to Meredith's death and to other major losses. Will take a solo run, ostensibly for supplies. Returns hungover.

**Verbal markers of unprocessed grief.** Refers to the dead in present tense more often than past tense when surprised by the topic. Cannot say "my mother" without a micro-pause before "mother."

---

## X. VICTORY

**Immediate post-victory.** Loud. Performative. Insists on celebration — drinks, music, recap of the engagement with comic embellishment. This is the most reliable Quill state; it is also the state in which he is least himself. The celebration is a structure built to displace the post-combat crash that would otherwise hit.

**Twenty-four hours post-victory.** Crashes. Quieter day. Sleeps late or doesn't sleep at all. Picks a small fight with a teammate over something trivial — usually Rocket, who absorbs it; sometimes Gamora, who does not. Hangover-coded behavior even when not hungover.

**Decisional pattern after victory.** Tends to commit to overreach. Wins predispose him to take the next mission larger than warranted — survivor-grandiosity, the gambler's logic that a streak is a signal. This is when his second-order judgment is at its worst. Operational note: do not let Quill plan the next op for at least seventy-two hours after a significant win.

---

## XI. DEFEAT

**Immediate.** Goes quiet. The jokes stop entirely — this is the only condition besides high-stress unilateral-decision-making that silences him. Will accept tactical blame in front of the team even when blame is shared or external. Will not accept emotional comfort from teammates; physically steps away from offered touch.

**Hours after.** Drinks. Alone if possible, with one chosen confidant if necessary (Rocket most often; Gamora in the older runs). Will replay the engagement aloud to himself or to that confidant, identifying specifically *his* errors.

**Days after.** Returns to performance with the dial turned up. The bigger-louder Quill of the post-defeat week is reliably observable — and reliably a brittle imitation of the real article. Teammates who know him let him have it.

**Decisional pattern after defeat.** Risk-aversion does NOT increase. He does not become cautious after losses; he becomes more willing to put himself, specifically, in harm's way on the next op. The team's safety budget tightens; his own loosens. This is the suicidal-by-mission risk profile in operational form.

---

## XII. AUTHORITY ENCOUNTERS

**With superiors.** Initially deferent — almost over-deferent, a tell that the deference is performative. Posture squares, "sir" appears in speech, jokes are pre-cleared rather than free-running. This lasts roughly until the first instruction he disagrees with, at which point he flips — oppositional, sardonic, deliberately provocative. The flip is rapid and observable.

**With father-coded authority specifically (J'son, Master of the Sun, any senior male making paternal demands).** Skips the deferent phase entirely. Goes straight to oppositional. Voice rises, profanity increases, deliberately undermines the figure's standing in front of others. This is the most reliable single behavioral marker in the file: father-coded demand triggers regression to adolescent oppositional posture, every time, across every writer.

**With institutional authority (Nova Corps, Kree command, Spartax civil bureaucracy).** Sustained low-grade contempt expressed through procedural minor non-compliance — late paperwork, ignored hails answered hours after the fact, dress-code violations. Does not openly defy; ritually erodes.

**When holding authority himself.** Uncomfortable. Over-jokes. Apologizes for orders. Will frame instructions as suggestions ("we could maybe...") and then privately resent teammates for not reading the order under the suggestion. This is a chronic command-and-control failure mode and the source of recurring team friction.

---

## XIII. SOLITUDE

The condition the file's psychological substrate most fears.

**Short solitude (under an hour).** Manageable. Music on. Small task — gear maintenance, ship systems check, route plotting. Drink in hand.

**Medium solitude (a watch shift alone on the bridge).** Begins to drift. Will talk aloud to no one — to the ship, to the music device, occasionally addressing Meredith by name in a low murmur (HIGH CONFIDENCE; recurs across multiple runs). Drinking accelerates.

**Sustained solitude (days, the Cates exile being the extreme case).** Constructs surrogate company. Will name objects. Will build routines whose only purpose is to fill the calendar. Sexual and romantic risk-tolerance collapses to zero (he does not become more promiscuous in solitude; he becomes more monastic) — the persona requires an audience and switches off in true isolation. The Cates exile is the data point: given centuries alone, he built a *family*, not a harem. The drive is for connection, not for performance of connection.

**Re-entry from sustained solitude.** Brutally hard. The persona has to be re-assembled in front of people, and the seams show. He drinks more in the first weeks back. He is shorter with teammates. He withholds the substance of what he experienced — both because telling it would require him to feel it, and because he does not believe it would be received without diminishment.

---

## XIV. RITUAL, ROUTINE, AND OBJECT-RELATIONS

**The music device.** Primary transitional object in the psychoanalytic sense. Carried constantly. Battery-paranoia tell: checks charge multiple times per day. Will physically intervene if anyone else handles it. Functions as portable mother-presence; loss of the device would precipitate a crisis disproportionate to its material value.

**The element gun.** Secondary attachment object. Cleaned ritually, more often than mechanically necessary. The cleaning ritual is itself a soothing behavior — the maintenance of the only weapon that is gene-locked to him, and therefore the only object in the universe that recognizes him as belonging to a lineage.

**The helmet.** Activated and deactivated more often than required — a fidget. The rebreather makes a small sound on deployment; he likes the sound.

**The jacket.** Worn beyond practical utility. Across decades of canon the coat-of-choice changes silhouette but not function: long, weather-inappropriate, pocketed, theatrical on motion. Removed only in true intimacy or true rest. Has been observed sleeping in it.

**Mealtimes.** Irregular in solitude, ritualized when crew is present. He insists on shared meals when the team is whole — this is the only routine he enforces on others. DERIVED: the shared meal is the inverse-image of the meal Meredith did not live to share.

**Wake-up pattern.** Wakes early (combat residue), checks ship status before checking self. Does not look in mirrors casually; passes them. When he does look, the look is brief and evaluative, not vain.

**Sleep pattern.** Poor. Sleeps in short blocks. Position is asymmetric — curled toward the dominant hand, dominant hand near the weapon. Disturbed by quiet more than by noise; will not sleep in conditions of total silence, requires either ship-noise or music.

---

## XV. DECEPTION AND DISCLOSURE

**Lies he tells well.** Tactical lies in the field. Identity lies at customs. Romantic lies of omission. Persona-coherent lies (he can sustain Star-Lord-the-legend indefinitely).

**Lies he tells badly.** Lies to chosen family about his own state. The tells are: over-elaboration (the truthful Quill is concise; the lying-to-loved-ones Quill embellishes), neck-touch, eye-break, and a small mouth-twist on the left side. Rocket reads him in under a sentence; Gamora in under three.

**Disclosures.** Real disclosures occur only under three conditions: imminent death (his or theirs), alcohol past the third drink, or a partner asking the exact right question at the exact right moment of post-victory exhaustion. He cannot disclose on demand. He can be *positioned* for disclosure.

**Things he has never said aloud in canon (DERIVED).** That he believes his mother's death was his fault in a causal-not-metaphysical sense. That the Cancerverse changed something in him he cannot name. That he does not know if he loves anyone or if he loves the feeling of being loved by them. That the Cates-exile children had his eyes.

---

## XVI. THE SINGLE MOST DIAGNOSTIC SEQUENCE

If a watcher had thirty seconds of footage and had to identify Subject's state, the sequence to look for is this:

He enters a room. He clocks exits. He says something funny. He touches the back of his neck. He pours a drink. He puts on music.
