He breaks promises to romantic partners not from indifference but because the persona cannot sustain the proximity those promises require, and he will not stop being the persona. The fracture is between his stated ethic of love and his unstated ethic of self-protection. The latter wins. Every time.

**Under suicidal-mission temptation.** The line between "self-sacrifice as duty" and "self-sacrifice as relief" is one he does not police. He will take the pin-the-bomb mission slightly too readily, and the team has, across multiple runs, had to argue him out of plans whose tactical justification is thinner than the emotional one. His code permits martyrdom in ways a healthier code would flag.

---

## 7. How The Code Has Shifted Over Time

The vector across the published canon is toward **narrower, quieter, more tired enforcement** of essentially the same rules.

**Englehart-era (1976).** The code is barely present. Young Peter is depicted as bitter, opportunistic, hostile. The Star-Lord vocation, conferred by the Master of the Sun, is the *importation* of an ethic — a mission given to a man who had none. The early Star-Lord stories show him learning what a moral floor is by being placed in situations that demand one. This is the foundation: a code grafted onto a wound, which then takes root.

**Cosmic-operative middle period (Annihilation, Conquest).** The code militarizes. Loyalty to unit becomes load-bearing. Restraint on civilians becomes operational discipline. The "I will not abandon a teammate" rule is forged here under conditions of overwhelming force; it is paid for in blood and survivor's guilt. After Conquest, the rule about unilateral leadership *for* the team — the dark twin of the loyalty rule — is also forged. Both halves of the lattice harden simultaneously.

**Founder era (Abnett & Lanning vol. 2).** The code is at its most assertive and its most fractured. He is leading, recruiting, building — and lying to his team to do it. The contradiction surfaces (Mantis reveal, team fracture) but he does not internalize the lesson. The code's permissive zone around "for their own good" is at its widest here.

**Bendis era.** The code goes performative. The roguish charm thickens, the rules thin, the broken promises pile up. He is still loyal in crisis, still moral on the floor — but the *daily* ethical hygiene (kept commitments, present-tense honesty, accountability to intimates) degrades visibly. This is the era of the hologram proposal and the abandoned presidency. The code holds at peak intensity and frays everywhere else.

**Duggan / Cates / post-exile.** The fundamental shift. The Pleasure Garden exile imposes subjective centuries of slow, domestic, parental life — exactly the conditions his code was *never designed for*. He marries, raises children, loses them, ages. Whatever he was upon return, his ethics have been forced through the one solvent they could not previously survive: peace. He emerges quieter. The performative permissive-zone behaviors thin out (less serial seduction, less bar-brawl provocation, less swagger). The drinking deepens; the jokes are slower; the floor is the same floor but he stands on it differently. The shift is not redemption; it is *attrition*. The code has not improved. The man has fewer resources to expend on the surrounding performance.

Subsequent runs show him exercising the code with what reads as fatigue rather than conviction. He still will not abandon a teammate; he just no longer pretends to enjoy the demonstration of it. The ethical floor is intact and the ethical ceiling has lowered — he is less likely to undertake the maximalist gesture, more likely to do the small right thing without fanfare.

---

## 8. Synthesis

Peter Quill operates a moral code he did not author, does not articulate, and would deny holding. It is built of inviolable wound-shaped reflexes (the protections, the loyalty, the floor on intimate violence and on truth about death), surrounded by a wide permissive zone (theft, lies to authority, sex, drink, killing in combat, and crucially deception of allies "for their own good"), and held together by a small set of self-narrated justifications that allow him to terminate ethical thought before it reaches the parts of his behavior he cannot afford to examine.

The code is most consistent in protection of others, least consistent in honesty with intimates, structurally vulnerable to paternal-authority triggers and to the temptation of sacrificial relief, and slowly attriting toward a quieter, less performative enforcement as the character ages and accumulates loss.

He is, by enacted behavior, a substantially more ethical man than he allows himself to be seen as. The performance of amoralism is itself a moral choice — a way of refusing the heroic frame so that failure within it cannot annihilate him. He has built an ethics designed to let him keep going. It works. It has cost him almost every form of intimate honesty a person can have, and it has saved a great many lives, including some of his own.

The file's working assessment: *the code is real, it is sturdy where it matters most, and it is being held up by a man who is tired*. Any longitudinal intervention should not aim to install ethics he already has. It should aim to relieve him of the performance that the ethics have, until now, required to survive.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: PETER JASON QUILL

Classification: Linguistic-behavioral subsection. Derived from direct dialogue evidence across Englehart (1976), Abnett & Lanning (2008-2010), Bendis (2013-2015), Humphries solo, Zdarsky solo, Duggan, Ewing, and Cates runs. Speech is treated here as somatic data: a man's mouth tells on him the way his hands do.

---

## 1. BASELINE REGISTER — THE "STAR-LORD VOICE"

Subject operates from a default speech register best described as **late-twentieth-century American vernacular weaponized for cosmic contexts**. The base layer is mid-American English, specifically Missouri-inflected — a flatness of vowel, a slight Midwest swallow of the terminal "g" (going → goin'), softening under stress into something more rural than his formal self-presentation would suggest. Under fatigue and especially under alcohol, the Midwestern substratum surfaces noticeably; he becomes more "Peter" and less "Star-Lord" in phonemic terms before he becomes so in content.

Layered on top of the base: a deliberately retrofitted **idiom drawn from 1970s and 1980s Earth pop culture** — film references, song lyrics quoted as if proverbs, brand names used as units of measure ("about a Big Mac's worth"), and a steady supply of similes built from materials no one around him has ever seen. This is not affectation; it is **a sealed time capsule of his mother**. Every Earth idiom he deploys is a piece of pre-loss vocabulary preserved in amber. He uses them in front of beings who cannot possibly get the reference because the reference is not for them. It is a private continuous channel to a dead woman, run in public.

Pitch sits in the upper-mid baritone, with a tendency to **rise at the end of declarative sentences** when he is performing — a borrowed interrogative lilt that invites collaboration and disarms hierarchy. When he is actually serious, the lilt drops out and the line ends flat or descending. This is one of the most reliable tells in his entire repertoire: *if Quill stops asking implicit permission at the end of his sentences, he is no longer playing.*

Volume modulation is wide. He is loud in groups, loud in bars, loud on bridges of ships when giving orders he is uncertain about. He is quiet in the rare scenes where he is alone with someone he has decided to trust. **Quiet Quill is rare Quill, and quiet Quill means something.**

---

## 2. THE PERSONA-NAME ANNOUNCEMENT — A LINGUISTIC PATHOGNOMONIC

The repeated, almost compulsive self-introduction — *"Star-Lord"*, with insistence on the dash, with offense taken when others mishear or shorten or refuse it — is the most diagnostically rich line he speaks. The behavior recurs across decades and writers, consistent enough to be considered a fixed verbal ritual.

Three things are happening simultaneously in that announcement:

1. **An assertion of identity to himself**, performed via others. He needs to hear the name in the room. The name in the room is evidence the persona is present.
2. **A pre-emptive frame.** By naming himself first he denies the interlocutor the opportunity to name him on their terms — to call him "the human," "the half-breed," "Meredith's boy," "J'son's son." He arrives pre-labeled.
3. **A small, repeated piece of restitution to his mother**, who named the persona in nursery form ("my little Star-Lord") and who is the only person who ever got to call him anything without his curating it.

The fact that he *takes offense* when corrected or mocked on the name is the data. Genuine grandiosity does not require defense; brittle compensation does. He is most fragile linguistically at the exact moment he is loudest.

---

## 3. HUMOR ARCHITECTURE — DEFLECTION ENGINEERED AT THE SENTENCE LEVEL

Humor is the load-bearing element of his speech and the primary affect-regulation tool described elsewhere in this file. At the linguistic level it has structure.

**Preferred forms:**

- **The pre-emptive self-deprecation**, deployed before anyone else can land the joke. ("Yeah, I know how that sounds. I was there when I said it.") Function: removes the wound's leverage by claiming it first.
- **The cosmic-banality juxtaposition.** He pairs a galactic referent with a domestic-American one ("a Celestial the size of, I dunno, Kansas"). Function: shrinks the unmanageable to mother-scale.
- **The misdirected referent.** Quotes a song or film at someone who can't possibly know it, then refuses to explain. Function: maintains a private register he controls; tests who in the room will laugh anyway on faith.
- **The deflated punchline.** Begins a serious sentence, swerves into a joke before it lands. ("My mother used to — you know what, never mind, who wants a drink.") Function: aborts vulnerability mid-syllable.
- **The escalating exaggeration**, especially under tactical pressure — every estimate gets larger, every danger gets named with a comic intensifier ("oh, that's bad, that's *species-extinction* bad"). Function: distributes the dread by spreading it across the sentence.

**Frequency rule:** humor density rises in direct proportion to felt threat or grief. The funniest scenes Quill speaks in are usually the saddest scenes he is in. If a clinician charted joke-rate against situational stakes, the curve would be positive and steep. **He is at his most verbally entertaining when he is closest to coming apart.**

---

## 4. PROFANITY, EXPLETIVE GRAMMAR, AND CODE-SHIFT

His profanity is workmanlike and patterned. Default register avoids the heaviest registers (mostly mid-grade — "hell," "damn," "crap," "son of a — "), with full deployment reserved for genuine alarm or genuine rage. **Profanity escalation in Quill is a reliable distress signal**; he does not casually swear at the top of the scale. When the worst words start arriving, the persona is no longer mediating.

He also code-shifts across alien vernaculars — light use of Kree military slang from his Conquest period, occasional Spartoi inflection (used sarcastically more than fluently), bar argot picked up across the Knowhere/Rajak/Kyln circuit. The translator implant makes this stylistic rather than necessary; he selects loanwords for *flavor*, the way one wears a souvenir. This is also tell-rich: when he drops a Spartoi term, he is usually thinking about his father whether or not the conversation is about him.

---

## 5. ENDEARMENTS, ADDRESS TERMS, AND THE ROSTER OF NICKNAMES

He nicknames compulsively. Almost no one in his orbit is addressed by their actual name once a familiarity threshold is crossed. Across runs: *Rocket* becomes "buddy," "pal," diminutives that the recipient resents and tolerates; *Gamora* gets soft variants ("Gam," and softer cooed forms in private); *Drax* gets earnest direct address (Drax does not accept ironic forms, and Quill, reading the room, adjusts); *Groot* is addressed in full unironic affection; *Mantis*, after the wipe incident and its long aftermath, is addressed with conspicuous formality — *her actual name, every time*, a linguistic act of penance.

**Diagnostic value of the nicknames:**

- He shortens names of those he is trying to close distance with. Closeness, for him, is a verbal act of *reduction*. The shortened name is a claim of intimacy he can make without negotiating consent.
- He uses full formal names when (a) he has wronged the person and is still atoning, (b) he is about to deliver bad news, or (c) he is angry and trying not to show it. The full name is a fence.
- He almost never uses his own full name aloud. "Peter Jason Quill" is something his mother said. To say it himself would be to summon her, which he will only do under extreme duress.

Romantic address terms are sentimental and dated — *sweetheart, darlin', baby, beautiful* — drawn from the same pre-1988 Earth vocabulary as his idioms. He is making love (and proposing) with his mother's lexicon, which is one reason it never quite works.

---

## 6. HOW HE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Love-language in Quill is a study in displacement.

He does not, in canonical evidence, say "I love you" easily, on time, or to the right person at the right moment. The phrase appears, but usually **late, hedged, or mediated** — by hologram (the Pryde proposal), by gesture, by reckless act, by the words of a song playing in the background while he says something adjacent. He prefers to **encode** affection.

Observable forms:

- **The shared reference.** Quoting a lyric or line that means something to him, watching to see if the other person receives it as more than nonsense. If they do, that is an "I love you."
- **The gift of music.** Sharing a tape, a track, a playlist — for him this is functionally a marriage proposal. Music is mother; mother is the thing he loved without ambivalence; sharing the channel is sharing her.
- **The protective interposition without comment.** He will physically step between a loved one and a threat and then refuse to discuss having done so afterward. The act is the sentence.
- **The nickname softening.** When the nickname for a partner gets quieter and shorter in private — that is the verbal correlate of dropped guard.
- **The chore.** Late in his timelines, especially post-Cates exile, affection migrates further into the domestic and pre-verbal — fixing the other person's ship subsystem without being asked, leaving the coffee analogue made. Words are still hard.

When he *does* say the thing directly, two markers tend to appear: a preceding swallow or hesitation (the persona stepping aside to let "Peter" speak), and a follow-up joke within two beats to seal the wound the directness opened. The joke is the bandage.

---

## 7. HOW HE COMMUNICATES THREAT

Threat-speech is the cleanest register he has and the one most consistent across writers. It is **quiet, declarative, short, and uses the actual name of the threatened party.**

Pattern features:

- Drop in volume rather than rise. He gets *softer* when he means it. Loud Quill is the persona; soft Quill is the gun.
- Loss of the interrogative lilt. Sentences end flat.
- Loss of contractions. ("You will not." rather than "You won't.") This is small and consistent across runs.
- Use of the second person paired with a precise consequence, no hyperbole. ("You touch her, I burn this station.") The shrinkage of comic exaggeration is the giveaway — under real threat, his metaphors become literal.
- Names rather than nicknames for the antagonist. The fence goes up.

**Threat-Quill speaks the way Persona-Quill cannot afford to speak the rest of the time.** If you have ever heard him level, you have met the man under the costume. Most people in his life have heard it two or three times across years.

---

## 8. HOW HE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

He does not, primarily. Grief in Quill is **encoded as absence in the speech stream** rather than expressed.

Markers:

- **The aborted sentence.** Begins to reference his mother, the Cancerverse, the Pleasure-Garden family, or any Annihilation-era casualty by name, and stops. Mid-clause. The unfinished sentence is where the grief lives.
- **The substitution.** Asked about a lost figure, he answers a slightly different question — replies to the question he wishes had been asked. This is consistent enough across runs to be a near-tic.
- **The retreat to lyric.** Quotes a song instead of answering. The song does the speaking. He gets to feel it without admitting he is feeling it.
- **The drink-as-punctuation.** A swallow takes the place of the next sentence. Conversational silence covered by physical motion.
- **The deflection to logistics.** "Anyway, we need to refuel" arriving as the conversational pivot at the exact moment a grief-laden topic threatens to land.
- **The very rare direct statement**, almost always when alone with one other person, almost always quiet, almost always followed by an immediate change of subject he himself enacts. He will not let another person attend his grief for more than a sentence at a time.

The Cates-exile material is a special case: he speaks about it almost not at all, and when he does, the diction becomes *generic* — abstractions, "a long time," "some people," refusing the proper nouns that would make it real. Specificity is where the hurt lives, and he refuses specificity. **What he will not name, he is still bleeding from.**

---

## 9. RHETORICAL STRUCTURE IN COMMAND CONTEXTS

When leading — bridge speech, mission briefing, pre-combat rallying — his rhetoric follows a recognizable shape:

1. **Open with a joke** to lower the room's pulse (and his own).
2. **State the situation in plain, slightly self-deprecating terms** ("Okay, so this is stupid, but here's what we're doing").
3. **Assign roles in second-person direct address**, using nicknames, fast.
4. **Close with a callback** — to a previous mission, to a shared joke, to a piece of music. The callback is the morale device; it converts a one-off into a chapter of an ongoing shared story.
5. **Almost never** acknowledge the possibility of failure aloud. He plans for it tactically; he refuses to *speak* it.

In contrast, his **post-mission debrief speech** is notably weaker. He resists structured retrospection. He prefers to convert the debrief into a drink. This is consistent with the larger pattern: he can speak forward into danger but cannot speak back into what happened.

---

## 10. SPEECH UNDER ALCOHOL

Distinct, well-documented across runs. Markers:

- **Midwest substratum surfaces** (phonemic flattening, "g"-drops, slower cadence).
- **Sentimentality rises**; he becomes more willing to speak love-adjacent material, though still indirectly.
- **The mother-channel opens slightly**: he is more likely to reference her in passing, though still in fragments.
- **Joke-rate paradoxically drops**; sober Quill jokes to deflect, drunk Quill has fewer defenses online and so jokes less. This is counterintuitive and reliable.
- **Sentences get longer and less edited**; he meanders.
- **He repeats himself** — same anecdote, same line, with the awareness of repetition suppressed.
- **Touch increases as speech decreases**; he becomes more physical, less verbal, as intake increases.

A practiced observer can read his intoxication level off his speech inside thirty seconds without seeing the glass.

---

## 11. SPEECH UNDER INTERROGATION OR CAPTIVE CONDITIONS

Tested by canon repeatedly. Pattern:

- **Talks more, not less.** Volume of speech is itself a tool — fills the room with noise, denies the interrogator a structured silence to work in.
- **Cycles through registers fast** — flirtation, mockery, faux-cooperation, sudden seriousness, joke — to prevent the interrogator from getting calibration on him.
- **Lies fluently about facts, poorly about feelings.** He can invent a cover story in real time. He cannot maintain emotional blankness about a loved one's name if it is invoked. *The pressure point a competent interrogator would find is relational, not informational.*
- **Will not curse out his captors past a certain threshold**, oddly — when conditions become genuinely dire, he becomes more formal, more contained. This connects to the threat-register pattern: real danger collapses the persona toward something quieter.

---

## 12. WRITTEN AND ASYNCHRONOUS COMMUNICATION

He is a worse writer than speaker. Logs, messages, recorded transmissions across runs show:

- A reflex toward the **flippant short form** — a one-liner where a paragraph is warranted.
- Avoidance of names in writing of grief-coded content (consistent with the spoken pattern).
- Use of recorded audio/holo messages where he could send text — he needs the performance medium; flat text strips his defenses.
- The hologram-proposal incident with Pryde is the paradigm case: maximum emotional content delivered through maximum mediating distance, in a register that lets him be *seen performing the feeling* without being present for the response. The medium was the symptom.

---

## 13. LINGUISTIC TELLS — CONSOLIDATED REGISTRY

For operational reference, the following tells are robust across runs and are flagged in roughly descending reliability:

1. **Drop in interrogative lilt → he is serious.**
2. **Loss of contractions → he means the threat.**
3. **Quieter and shorter sentences in combat speech → maximum lethality.**
4. **Full-formal use of someone's name → either penance, fence, or imminent bad news.**
5. **Mid-clause aborted sentence about a lost person → active grief breakthrough; conversation will pivot in two beats.**
6. **Sudden Midwest phoneme drift → fatigue, alcohol, or unguarded affection.**
7. **Reference-density spike → felt threat or felt grief, look for which.**
8. **Song-quotation in lieu of answer → emotional content he refuses to render in his own words.**
9. **Insistence on the "Star-Lord" name at unusual intensity → ego-fragility spike; the persona feels threatened in that scene.**
10. **Conversational pivot to logistics ("anyway, we need to —") → he just felt something and is moving away from it.**
11. **Spartoi loanword → his father is in his head whether or not in the conversation.**
12. **Spoken use of his own full name → catastrophic stress; the mother-channel is fully open.**

---

## 14. SYNTHESIS

Subject's speech is a precision-engineered defense system retrofitted from his mother's vocabulary and his own subsequent decades of cosmic exposure. The persona-voice — loud, lilting, joke-dense, reference-laden, nickname-happy — exists to do the work that his interior cannot do unaided: regulate affect, manage distance, summon the dead, command rooms he does not feel qualified for, and outrun the silence in which grief catches him.

The voice is dense with tells precisely *because* it is doing so much work. A system that complex cannot be perfectly maintained; the seams show, and they show in patterned, readable ways. To listen carefully to Peter Quill speak is to hear two people at once — the boy who lost his mother and the man he built to carry the boy — and to notice, across any sustained conversation, which of them currently has the microphone.

He is, linguistically, a man **talking continuously so as not to be alone in the room with himself**. The silences are where he lives. The speech is where he hides.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward inference engine. Format: GIVEN a stimulus or context the canon has not depicted, EXPECT the following behavior, with reasoning anchored in the established profile (C-PTSD primary, AUD moderate, attachment disorganized, persona as load-bearing costume). Confidence calibrated. This section maps the daily texture — the granular surface a total-surveillance file would catch on hour 4,000 of observation, not hour four.*

---

## A. Diurnal & Solitary Routine

**GIVEN** an unstructured morning aboard the Milano (or equivalent vessel) with no mission queued — **EXPECT** the following ordered sequence, ±15 minutes: wake later than he claims to wake; lie in the bunk for between four and eleven minutes in what an observer would code as "thinking" but is closer to inventorying which losses are loudest today; reach for a device (Walkman, Zune, equivalent audio cache) *before* reaching for water, clothing, or weapon; play a track from a tight rotation of roughly forty songs his mother liked, never on shuffle of the full library, always within that core forty; brush teeth and dress in the same order every day (boots last — he leaves them by the bunk and steps into them already half-out the door, a habit fossilized from foster placements where you slept in case you had to run). Coffee or its alien equivalent within the first twenty minutes; the first words spoken aloud are almost always to a teammate or to the ship, not to himself — solitary verbal self-talk is rare because silence-with-self is the thing being avoided. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a night alone, no mission, no company — **EXPECT** drinking. Not crisis drinking; ritual drinking. Two to five units across three to five hours, paced by music. He will reorganize a small thing (a drawer, a tool kit, the contents of his jacket pockets) for forty minutes as a way of justifying being awake. Late in the evening he will play one specific song he does not play in company. He will not cry, or not predictably; what happens is closer to a long exhale that lasts an hour. He sleeps in his clothes when alone more often than not. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an unexpected gift of fully unstructured time — say, a week of mandated leave — **EXPECT** failure to use it as intended. By day two he will have invented a small project (ship repair, a "favor" for a contact, a side errand framed as decompression). The unstructured week becomes a structured week in which the structure is self-imposed busywork. This is the avoidance-via-mobility defense reasserting itself; stillness is the threat his entire architecture was built to keep at bay. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a forced medical hold (injured, grounded, told to rest) — **EXPECT** escalating restlessness within 36 hours; minor rule-breaking by hour 60 (walking on the injury, lifting things he was told not to lift); flirtation with whoever staffs the medbay as a way of metabolizing the powerlessness through performance; and, if confinement extends past four days, a sharp uptick in drinking and a dip into the quieter, glibness-stripped register that teammates have learned to read as warning. *Confidence: high.*

---

## B. Sleep, Dreams, Startle

**GIVEN** sleep onset in an unfamiliar room — **EXPECT** weapon within arm's reach (element gun under pillow or on adjacent surface, oriented grip-toward-dominant-hand); door checked twice; one light source identified as "the one I kill last." Sleep latency 25–60 minutes; he uses music or low ambient noise to bridge it. *Confidence: very high — battlefield-trained behavior, persistent across decades.*

**GIVEN** an unexpected loud noise during sleep — **EXPECT** waking to full motor readiness within 1.5 seconds; weapon acquired before eyes are fully focused; *no* verbal challenge in the first three seconds (he assesses silently — a habit consistent with not wanting to announce himself to a hostile in the dark). He then over-corrects with a joke once threat is ruled out. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate touching his shoulder from behind without speaking — **EXPECT** a brief but observable startle (shoulder hitch, breath catch, half-step pivot), instantly converted into a grin and a quip. The conversion is so fast most observers code it as theatrical greeting and miss the startle entirely. Surveillance-grade observation would catch it every time. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** dream content (inferred from canon trauma load) — **EXPECT** recurrent imagery of his mother's hospital room or the night of her death; the Cancerverse (formless, organic, wrong-lit); the Pleasure-Garden family aging and disappearing. He does not report these. If asked about dreams he will lie pleasantly or change the subject with a joke about a sex dream. *Confidence: moderate-to-high on content; very high on non-disclosure.*

---

## C. Eating, Drinking, Consumption

**GIVEN** a shared meal with the team — **EXPECT** he eats fast, talks more than he eats, refills others' cups before his own (charm gesture, also control gesture — he likes being the one pouring), and finishes last because he has been performing host. He picks at food when alone and overeats in company; the social context is the appetite. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an unfamiliar alien cuisine of dubious safety — **EXPECT** he tries it first, before anyone else, with theatrical commentary. This is bravado but also caretaking: he would rather be the one poisoned than watch a teammate be the one poisoned. The pattern is a micro-version of the suicide-by-mission tendency in low-stakes form. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** access to Earth food he has not had in years (peanut butter, a specific candy, a soda) — **EXPECT** disproportionate emotional response, hidden under a "this is amazing" grin. He will hoard the remainder. He will share one piece with the teammate he most wants to bond with that week. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a bar in a port city, no mission — **EXPECT** he scans the room within four seconds of entry (exits, threats, alone-women, alone-men of size, bartender disposition); chooses a seat with back-to-wall and sight-line to the door; orders something he has had before in similar establishments; tips immediately and well (rapport investment, also escape insurance). He drinks faster than the people he is with and pretends to be at their pace by ordering a second when they are still on their first. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a drink offered by a stranger — **EXPECT** he accepts but does not drink it until he has watched the bartender pour another for someone else from the same bottle, or until he has subtly switched glasses. Smuggler's reflexes, intact. *Confidence: high.*

---

## D. Music, Audio, Sensory Anchors

**GIVEN** any moment of transition (entering a ship, leaving a planet, beginning a mission, finishing one) — **EXPECT** music cued within ninety seconds. The audio device is functionally a prosthetic regulator of his nervous system. He does not narrate this; it is so habituated that he would not notice doing it. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** damage to or theft of his primary audio device — **EXPECT** disproportionate distress, anger out of scale to the object's monetary or tactical value, and a recovery operation prioritized above mission logic. Teammates who have seen this twice have learned not to touch the device. The device is mother-coded; harming it is harming her, again. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a song from his core rotation playing unexpectedly in a public space (some alien bar with improbable curation, a salvaged Earth jukebox) — **EXPECT** he freezes for one to three seconds; face slackens; then he covers with a comment like "oh man" and tries to play it as joyful nostalgia. The freeze is the tell. He will drink more that night. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** silence imposed (stealth ops, library, hospital quiet) — **EXPECT** subvocal humming, finger-tapping rhythm on his thigh or weapon, or chewing the inside of his cheek. Some external rhythm is always running. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## E. Speech Patterns, Verbal Tics, Conversational Choreography

**GIVEN** an introduction to a stranger — **EXPECT** he announces "Star-Lord" before the stranger asks. If the stranger has not heard the name, he tells the story of the name. If the stranger has heard it and is unimpressed, he laughs *first*, beating them to the joke. The persona is announced because it must be witnessed to function. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a sincere compliment — **EXPECT** deflection via self-deprecating joke within three seconds. He does not know how to receive praise except by neutralizing it. If the complimenter persists, he changes the subject or makes physical contact (shoulder clap, fist bump) to end the exchange kinetically. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a sincere personal question ("are you okay," "what happened to you in there," "do you miss her") — **EXPECT** one of three responses, in declining order of frequency: (1) a joke that is not quite an answer; (2) a partial true answer followed immediately by a deflection ("yeah, anyway —"); (3) silence followed by leaving the room. He almost never gives the full answer in the moment; if he ever does, it is hours later, in motion (working on the ship, walking back from a bar), to one specific person, not the asker. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he uses an Earth idiom no one understands — **EXPECT** he over-explains the reference with visible pleasure. Earth pop-culture exposition is one of his few unmasked behaviors; he is genuinely delighted to be the only person in a room who knows the thing. This is the boy from Missouri leaking through. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he is corrected in front of others on a factual matter — **EXPECT** he concedes with a joke that absorbs the loss ("yeah, okay, fair, you're the smart one, I'm just the handsome one"). He does not litigate. The concession is real; the joke covers the small sting. If corrected by a *romantic interest*, he concedes faster and warmer. If corrected by a *father-coded authority*, he resists. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he is interrupted while telling a story — **EXPECT** mild irritation masked, the story abandoned rather than restarted. He will not insist on the floor. This is the foster-kid economy of attention: do not push, you do not get to push. *Confidence: moderate-to-high.*

**Verbal tics catalogued:** "man" as filler; the upward-inflected "okay—" used to reset a tense moment; "look,—" as preface to a serious sentence (signal that the next sentence is real); calling teammates by diminutives or invented nicknames as a claim of intimacy; sing-song repetition of someone's name when he wants something. He swears situationally rather than habitually — his swearing escalates as stress escalates, which makes it a usable affect gauge. *Confidence: high.*

---

## F. Body, Posture, Micro-movement

**GIVEN** standing in a neutral conversation — **EXPECT** weight on one leg, hands occupied (in pockets, on belt, holding something), one shoulder slightly lower than the other (old combat injury legacy, probably left side per Conquest-era damage). He gestures with open palms when persuading, closed fists when frustrated, and touches his own face — jaw, back of neck — when lying or when caught in a true feeling he does not want to show. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he is seated — **EXPECT** he sprawls. Legs wide, one arm over the back of the adjacent seat. Sprawl is territorial display and also a non-defensive posture announcement: *I am relaxed, you should be relaxed.* When he is actually relaxed the sprawl narrows; when he is performing relaxation it widens. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he enters a room — **EXPECT** a one-second pause at the threshold to scan, then a deliberate loose-limbed walk-in that reads as casual. The pause is invisible to most. He counts exits without knowing he is counting. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** he is lying — **EXPECT** sustained eye contact (overcorrection; he knows liars look away, so he doesn't), slight increase in smile, and a hand gesture that opens away from his body as if presenting the lie like a small gift. Truths are told with less eye contact and fewer gestures. *Confidence: moderate-to-high — the pattern is consistent but not 100%.*

**GIVEN** physical proximity to an attractive person — **EXPECT** a slight forward lean, micro-orientation of the torso, voice drop by a quarter-octave. Flirtation is so habituated it activates without intent; he flirts with bartenders he will never see again because flirting is how he says hello to the world. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** physical proximity to a child — **EXPECT** he goes into a crouch to be at their eye level, his voice softens by a measurable degree, and his hands go where the child can see them. This is one of the few unstudied tendernesses he displays. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** physical proximity to an elderly woman who resembles, in any feature, his mother — **EXPECT** brief disorientation, a longer-than-necessary politeness, and an inability to leave the interaction without offering some small help (carrying something, fixing something). He will not name why. *Confidence: moderate-to-high.*

---

## G. Money, Possessions, Tools

**GIVEN** an unexpected payout from a job — **EXPECT** he spends roughly a third inside 72 hours (drinks, gear upgrades, gifts for teammates that are framed as practical but are emotionally communicative), banks none, hides a small reserve in two or three caches the team does not know about. The caches are not for him; they are for them, in case he is not there. He would not phrase it that way. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an unexpected financial loss — **EXPECT** performative shrug, internal recalculation, and a small uptick in risk-taking on the next job to compensate. He does not budget; he replaces. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** any tool or object he has owned for more than a year — **EXPECT** he can field-strip and reassemble it without looking; he is sentimental about objects in a way he does not allow himself to be about people. He talks to the ship. He has named the element gun, probably more than once. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** loss of a sentimental object — **EXPECT** distress disproportionate to the object, brief; then he replaces it badly and pretends the replacement is fine; the loss is logged internally on a growing list. *Confidence: moderate.*

---

## H. Romantic & Sexual Conduct

**GIVEN** first contact with a new romantic interest — **EXPECT** rapid escalation in the first 72 hours (charm, attentiveness, the full bandwidth of his social skill), followed by a plateau, followed by a manufactured reason he must be elsewhere within two to six weeks. The exit is rarely clean and never sit-down; it is logistical ("the job ran long," "the team needed me"). *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a romantic interest who refuses to be charmed — **EXPECT** increased interest. Resistance reads to him as honesty, and honesty is the rare currency. A partner who sees through him is more compelling than one who buys the act, even though the seeing-through is exactly what will eventually make him flee. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a romantic interest he is genuinely falling for — **EXPECT** he becomes *less* glib in their presence over time, not more; the joke rate drops; he asks more questions than he answers. This is the tell that distinguishes a real bond from a habituated performance. The same person will also be the one he is most absent from. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** the morning after a casual encounter — **EXPECT** he leaves before the other person wakes, or stays and makes breakfast as a kindness that is also a goodbye. He does not do mornings-after with talking. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he is asked to define a relationship — **EXPECT** evasion, humor, or an over-grand gesture that substitutes for definition (a gift, a trip, a hologram proposal). He cannot do the small ordinary verbal commitment; he can do the spectacular one because the spectacular one is still a performance. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an ex re-enters his life — **EXPECT** unfinished-ness floods back; he is warm, useful, present for the duration of whatever brought them together; and he is incapable of either getting back together cleanly or letting go cleanly. *Confidence: high.*

---

## I. Friendship & Team Texture

**GIVEN** a teammate is injured — **EXPECT** he is the first to the medbay, makes jokes the injured teammate must respond to (which is its own diagnostic), stays longer than necessary, and *does not* discuss the injury later. The presence is the apology for an inability to discuss. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate's birthday or analogous milestone — **EXPECT** he remembers, sometimes belatedly, and overcompensates with a gift that is too thoughtful — he listened, weeks ago, when the teammate mentioned wanting something, and he tracked it down. He will frame the gift as no big deal. The gift is the apology for the lateness, which is the symptom of the chronic-lateness pattern, which is the symptom of the deeper avoidance. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate confides a problem — **EXPECT** he listens better than his persona suggests he would; he asks one or two real questions; he offers a solution rather than sitting in the feeling (this is his limit), and he privately tries to fix the problem off-screen without telling them. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate confronts him about his own behavior — **EXPECT** initial deflection (joke, then minimization), then if the teammate persists past the second deflection, a flash of irritation, then if they persist past that, a quiet capitulation that is more about ending the conversation than about agreement. Actual behavioral change follows only if the confronting teammate is one of two or three people whose judgment he weights heavily — and even then it lasts six to ten weeks before drifting back. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** internal team conflict not involving him — **EXPECT** he attempts mediation with humor first, then with a "look,—" speech, then with a unilateral decision that ends the argument by removing its object. He cannot tolerate intra-family strife for long; it activates the dissolution fear. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a teammate leaves the Guardians — **EXPECT** outward warmth, "we'll see you soon," a joke. Internally: catastrophic. He will drink that night. He will not be the one to call them in the months after; he will not call because he is afraid they will not call back, which would confirm something he cannot afford to confirm. *Confidence: very high.*

---

## J. Strangers, Crowds, Public Conduct

**GIVEN** a crowded market or public square — **EXPECT** he reads the crowd continuously; he is friendly to vendors, generous with small currency, attentive to children and elderly, polite to the point of warmth with service workers (foster-kid solidarity — he knows who gets ignored). He is rude only to people who are rude first, and the rudeness is performative more than felt. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** a beggar or someone in obvious need — **EXPECT** he gives, often more than he should, often without comment. He does not perform the charity. This is one of his cleanest moral reflexes. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** witnessing a parent shouting at a child in public — **EXPECT** observable stillness, jaw set, hands flexing. He may or may not intervene depending on severity; if he does, he intervenes with humor first as de-escalation. If the parent escalates physically, the intervention becomes immediate and not humorous. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an authority figure (port officer, customs, local enforcement) asks for ID — **EXPECT** charm-first compliance theater, paperwork that is mostly real and slightly forged, a joke that humanizes him to the officer, and a clean exit. If the officer is rigid or contemptuous, the charm sharpens into something subtly mocking that the officer often will not catch. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** being recognized in public (someone says "you're Star-Lord") — **EXPECT** delight visible for a fraction of a second, then practiced modesty ("well, I mean—"), then engagement with the fan/recognizer at a rate proportional to how lonely he is that week. He will sign a thing if asked. He will remember this encounter and reference it later as if it were a small joke; it was not. *Confidence: high.*

---

## K. Technology, Information, Communication

**GIVEN** a new comm device, ship system, or interface — **EXPECT** he learns it by use, not by manual; he is competent within an hour, expert within a week, and has customized the interface within a month (his own shortcuts, his own audio cues). He never reads documentation. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** an unanswered message from a non-team contact — **EXPECT** delay measured in days to weeks. Reply, when it comes, is warm and apologetic and proposes a future contact that may or may not occur. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** an unanswered message from a team member — **EXPECT** response within hours, usually within one. The two tiers of contact are visible in the latency data alone. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** a private channel for confidential information — **EXPECT** he secures it adequately, then forgets to update credentials; smuggler's discipline is real but inconsistent. He is more careful with others' secrets than his own. *Confidence: moderate-to-high.*

---

## L. Calendar, Memory, Anniversaries

**GIVEN** the anniversary of his mother's death — **EXPECT** he does not name it. He is quieter that day; he drinks earlier; he is gentler with the team and less available to strangers. He will play one specific song in private. If a teammate asks what is wrong, he will say "nothing" with a smile that is almost convincing. *Confidence: very high.*

**GIVEN** the anniversary of a comparable loss (Cancerverse return date, Conquest team's death, the loss of his Pleasure-Garden family) — **EXPECT** similar muted pattern. He does not commemorate; he survives the day. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** Earth holidays (Christmas, especially) — **EXPECT** disproportionate sentiment, often performed as kitsch to make it bearable. He will try to organize a celebration aboard ship and will be both delighted and undone by it. *Confidence: high.*

**GIVEN** he is asked his own birthday — **EXPECT** he gives the date easily but rarely celebrates it. Birthdays are mother-coded; she is the one who would have made the day. *Confidence: moderate-to-high.*

---

## M. The Aggregate Texture

What the longitudinal observation file shows, across thousands of small data points,


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Behavioral forecasting under load. Each entry: a specified stimulus (GIVEN), the predicted behavioral cascade (EXPECT), with confidence calibration and the canonical evidence base. Predictions are organized from acute external threat through interpersonal betrayal into the deep-wound zone where the persona fails and the child underneath becomes briefly visible.*

---

## A. Acute External Threat — Tactical Crisis

### A.1 — Ambush / outnumbered firefight

**GIVEN:** Team is jumped in a confined environment (corridor, cantina, hangar bay), enemies outnumber by ≥3:1, allies present.

**EXPECT:** Verbal output spikes *before* weapons output. He will quip into the opening exchange — a beat of audible mockery aimed at the largest or most-armored opponent — and only then begin shooting. The quip is not decoration; it is targeting. It buys him the half-second to read the room, locate exits, and identify which teammate is most exposed. He will then move *toward* the most exposed teammate, not toward the best cover. Element gun used at mid-range, jet boots engaged only when vertical advantage or a body-extraction is required (he conserves boot-burn; it is the gear he treats with the most operational respect). Calls targets aloud in a clipped shorthand he does not use in non-combat speech. Confidence: high. Pattern stable from Annihilation through Cates.

### A.2 — Solo, cornered, low ammunition

**GIVEN:** Separated from team, element gun depleted or jammed, hostile force closing.

**EXPECT:** Bargaining attempt first — not from cowardice but from instinct that a conversation buys options. He will offer information, a name, a relic location, *anything* that resembles trade. If bargaining fails within ~two exchanges he will switch hard: improvise an environmental weapon (decompression, ignition source, structural failure), accept significant collateral risk to himself, and exit through whatever opening the chaos creates. He does NOT freeze. He does NOT surrender. Surrender is the one childhood behavior he has trained out of himself. Confidence: high.

### A.3 — Team member down, conscious, bleeding out in his sightline

**GIVEN:** Visible casualty, recoverable, under fire.

**EXPECT:** Total tactical override. He will run the wrong way through fire to reach the body. Will not wait for cover. Will speak to the wounded teammate in a voice register markedly lower and slower than his combat voice — a "stay with me" cadence that is one of the few non-performed vocal modes he has. Will refuse to leave the body even if continued presence endangers extraction. If forced to choose between mission objective and casualty retrieval he chooses casualty retrieval ~9/10 times. This is non-negotiable behavior; the mother-shielding-child template is fully active. Confidence: very high.

### A.4 — Civilian children present in combat zone

**GIVEN:** Non-combatant minor(s) in danger, parent absent or dead.

**EXPECT:** Mission discipline collapses. He will absorb the child as a personal protection assignment regardless of objective. Will hand the child off only to someone he has personally vetted. Voice softens; he kneels to eye level; uses the child's name repeatedly if known. Post-engagement he will check on the child before checking on his own injuries. If the child has just witnessed a parent's death his behavior becomes near-religious in its focus — he is, structurally, attending to himself across time. Confidence: very high. Pressure point flagged in Section 5 confirmed operationally here.

### A.5 — Hostage situation, hostage is romantic partner or close teammate

**GIVEN:** Person he loves held at gunpoint, demands made.

**EXPECT:** He will comply *visibly* and deceive *invisibly*. Hands up, weapons surrendered, conversational, ingratiating — while routing every cognitive resource to the one-shot solution. Will accept terms he has no intention of honoring. If the hostage-taker invokes Peter's personal history to leverage compliance (the mother, the father, the Cancerverse, the Garden), behavior bifurcates: surface compliance deepens; internal lethality finalizes. Hostage-takers who name his wound aloud have, in his operational logic, just classified themselves as not-leaving-alive. Confidence: high.

---

## B. Catastrophic / Existential Stress

### B.1 — Universe-scale threat, conventional options exhausted

**GIVEN:** Cosmic-tier crisis, no clean tactical solution, a self-sacrificial option exists.

**EXPECT:** He volunteers. Not after deliberation — *during* the briefing. He will frame the offer as casual ("I've got this one"), make a joke about retirement, and begin moving toward the operational position before consensus forms. This is the Cancerverse template and it is reproducible. The volunteering is not heroic in his internal economy; it is *restful*. The suicide-mission slot is, for him, the one role in which the persona and the man briefly align — both the showman and the grieving boy agree that this is what he is for. Allies who recognize the pattern and intervene should EXPECT him to be furious with them afterward in inverse proportion to how grateful he should be. Confidence: very high.

### B.2 — Forced choice between two loved persons

**GIVEN:** Trolley-problem scenario, both targets are chosen-family.

**EXPECT:** He will attempt a third option past the point of viability. Will lie to himself about timeline. Will burn his own body (boots, gun overload, physical insertion) to manufacture an option that does not exist. If the choice cannot be evaded he will make it and not speak of it again — ever, to anyone. Will drink heavily for an extended period afterward. Will perform recovery within ~two weeks for the team's benefit; actual recovery does not occur. The unprocessed event becomes another stratum in the grief stack. Confidence: high.

### B.3 — Capture and interrogation, prolonged

**GIVEN:** Held by competent hostile intelligence apparatus, isolated, time-extended.

**EXPECT:** Phase 1 (0-12 hours): high verbal output, jokes, mock-cooperation, deliberate misdirection wrapped in plausible cadence. He is good at this; the translator-implant childhood means he has unusual confidence improvising under linguistic stress. Phase 2 (12-72 hours): verbal output decreases; cooperative posture maintained but information yield drops; he begins inventorying the room for exit vectors with a patience he does not display in normal life. Phase 3 (72+ hours): if physical torture begins, he becomes *quieter*, not louder — a notable inversion of his baseline. The persona has nothing to do here; it shuts off. Will sing under his breath (mother-era pop) as self-regulation; this is a tell. Will not break on operational intelligence; will break, eventually, on personal disclosures about teammates if those disclosures are framed as protective. Captors who threaten his people get more from him than captors who threaten him. Confidence: moderate-to-high.

### B.4 — Confronted with reality-warping or memory-altering attack

**GIVEN:** Telepath, illusionist, or reality-manipulator targets his mind.

**EXPECT:** Disproportionate, near-phobic resistance. The Mantis incident sits on both sides of this — he weaponized memory alteration and has therefore catalogued exactly how violating it is. Expect him to identify mental intrusion faster than baseline (he knows the texture), and to respond with lethal intent rather than capture intent. Telepaths are, in his threat-assessment heuristic, a separate category from other hostiles. He distrusts even allied telepaths with a residue that never fully dissolves. Confidence: high.

### B.5 — Confronted with a constructed paradise / wish-fulfillment trap

**GIVEN:** Hostile environment offering him an idealized reality (mother alive, family intact, exile-family restored, Garden returned).

**EXPECT:** This is his most dangerous scenario and the one in which his judgment is least reliable. The Cates exile demonstrated that he can build a life inside a closed loop and stay. EXPECT initial recognition of the trap (he is not stupid; the seams are visible to him), followed by a phase of *deliberate non-investigation* — he will avoid looking too closely at the seams because looking will require leaving. Extraction by teammates may require physical force. He will resent the rescuers for weeks. The fantasy that wounds him most is not the mother-restored one; it is the *Garden-restored* one, because that grief has no witnesses and the trap offers witnesses. Confidence: high.

---

## C. Betrayal — Concentric Rings

### C.1 — Betrayal by a peripheral ally (contact, fence, informant)

**GIVEN:** A working relationship of convenience double-crosses him.

**EXPECT:** Low affect. He absorbs it as cost-of-business. Will joke about it within the hour. May actually be impressed by a clever betrayal and reference it admiringly later. Retaliation, if any, is proportionate and unhurried. This is his healthiest interpersonal register precisely because nothing is at stake. Confidence: high.

### C.2 — Betrayal by a romantic partner

**GIVEN:** Lover deceives him materially (information, fidelity, loyalty to a hostile party).

**EXPECT:** Conspicuous performance of *not minding*. He will be charming, gracious, even self-deprecating about it ("had it coming"). Will exit the relationship cleanly and quickly. Will not pursue confrontation. The damage is real and deferred — manifests as increased drinking, a 2-4 week period of elevated sexual acting-out with strangers, and a hardening of the deflection layer for the next attempted intimacy. He does not let romantic betrayal *land* in real time because landing it would require a coherent self-narrative as someone worth being faithful to, which he does not reliably hold. Confidence: high.

### C.3 — Betrayal by a Guardian / core teammate

**GIVEN:** Founding-circle teammate acts against him or the team's stated mission.

**EXPECT:** Visible disproportion. Anger arrives fast and loud, then collapses into wounded confusion within a single conversation. He will demand explanation in a register that is uncharacteristically direct — the persona thins. Will not deploy humor here; the absence of jokes in a Quill confrontation is itself diagnostic of how deeply he is hurt. Reconciliation is possible but requires the betrayer to make the first move *and* to accept that Peter will not forget; he will reference the event obliquely in jokes for years. The team is the only structure he has built from scratch as an adult; threats to it metabolize as threats to the entire post-Meredith self-construction. Confidence: very high.

### C.4 — Betrayal that mirrors his own Mantis-incident pattern

**GIVEN:** A teammate makes a unilateral decision "for the team's own good," deceiving the group.

**EXPECT:** This is the single betrayal he cannot tolerate cleanly. Not because the act is uniquely heinous but because it is *his*. Reaction will be excessive, moralizing, near-self-righteous — and he will know, mid-reaction, that he is in bad faith, which makes him angrier. May escalate to expelling the offending teammate temporarily. Will reconcile later with private acknowledgment of the parallel; rarely with public acknowledgment. Pressure-point confirmed: being lied to "for his own good" is the betrayal that activates the deepest defenses fastest. Confidence: very high.

### C.5 — Betrayal by a father-coded figure

**GIVEN:** An authority figure he has provisionally trusted (mentor, commander, Spartoi official, J'son or analog) reveals manipulation or self-interest.

**EXPECT:** Splitting. The idealization collapses to devaluation in a single beat. Behavior shifts to oppositional-bitter for the remainder of the interaction and often the remainder of the relationship. Will sever contact rather than negotiate. Will weaponize the severance — refuses calls, refuses messages, refuses funeral attendance. The father-template is precommitted to disappointing him; confirmation merely closes a loop he had open. Confidence: very high.

### C.6 — Betrayal by Gamora specifically

**GIVEN:** Gamora acts against him or against the team in a way that implicates her loyalty.

**EXPECT:** Distinct from C.3. He will protect her *publicly* even while privately devastated. Will manufacture rationalizations for her behavior that he would not extend to others. Will attempt to recover the relationship past the point where the relationship is recoverable. This is the closest he gets to repeating his mother-shielding-child template in adult relational form — the assassin's daughter is, in his unconscious, both the most dangerous partner he could choose and therefore the most thoroughly chosen. Confidence: high.

### C.7 — Discovery that a longtime ally has been a deep-cover hostile from the beginning

**GIVEN:** A relationship he believed foundational was strategic deception throughout.

**EXPECT:** Catatonic-flavored shock for hours rather than minutes. Verbal output drops near zero. Will leave the room. Will drink alone. Will not retaliate immediately — possibly not for weeks. When retaliation comes it will be cold, planned, and unlike his usual improvisational signature. This is the betrayal pattern that produces his most uncharacteristic behavior, because it requires him to question the founding event of his post-Meredith life: *can chosen family be chosen, or was the choice an illusion all along?* If the answer destabilizes, everything destabilizes. Confidence: moderate (low base rate, but pattern in adjacent canonical events is consistent).

---

## D. Temptation

### D.1 — Offered restoration of mother

**GIVEN:** A power, entity, or technology credibly offers to return Meredith Quill.

**EXPECT:** He will refuse — *eventually*, and at cost. The refusal is canonically and characterologically certain (he has internalized that she died for him, and to undo it is to undo the meaning he has stacked on her death). But the refusal will not be clean. He will negotiate. He will ask questions he should not ask. He will require physical separation from the offering entity to reach the refusal. Anyone present who suggests acceptance casually will receive a response disproportionate to their offense. Post-refusal he will be unreachable for days. Confidence: very high.

### D.2 — Offered restoration of the Garden family

**GIVEN:** Same structure as D.1, applied to the Cates-exile family.

**EXPECT:** This refusal is *not* certain. The Garden grief is younger, less mythologized, more raw, and unwitnessed — which means the meaning-scaffolding he built around Meredith's death has not had time to form around the Garden losses. He may accept. He may accept and lie about it. He may accept and disappear from the Guardians without notice. This is, predictively, the single greatest defection risk in his profile. Confidence: moderate-high; flagged as the highest-priority watch condition.

### D.3 — Offered a kingdom / sovereignty / institutional power

**GIVEN:** Spartax throne, command of a fleet, governorship of a sector.

**EXPECT:** He will accept, briefly, theatrically, and then either abandon or sabotage the position within months. The Spartax presidency is the template. He cannot tolerate the *day-to-day* of held power because held power requires sitting still and being known. He will frame the eventual abdication as principled disagreement; the underlying mechanism is intimacy avoidance scaled up to institutional level. Confidence: very high.

### D.4 — Offered a clean exit (quiet life, sufficient wealth, no further obligations)

**GIVEN:** Genuine retirement option, no strings.

**EXPECT:** Considers it more seriously than he lets on. Will not take it. The persona requires audience; the man requires the team; the wound requires motion. A quiet life is, for him, the condition under which the unprocessed grief catches up. He has correctly intuited that he might not survive it. Confidence: high.

### D.5 — Offered an opportunity to murder a specific enemy with impunity

**GIVEN:** A figure responsible for one of his catastrophic losses is delivered to him, defenseless.

**EXPECT:** Will not do it. Will want to. Will perform reluctance less than he feels reluctance — the joke layer will fall away and he will look smaller than usual for a moment. Will demand the figure be turned over to a process he does not actually believe in, because believing in process is one of the structural lies he uses to remain someone Meredith would have recognized. Confidence: high. Note: this is one of the few scenarios in which his moral floor is *more* reliable than his rhetoric suggests.

### D.6 — Offered membership in an elite "above the team" structure

**GIVEN:** Invitation to a higher-tier cosmic organization (Annihilators-style, council-tier) that would elevate him out of the Guardians.

**EXPECT:** Flattered, briefly. Declines. May serve in dual capacity for a while and then quietly let the elevated role lapse. The Guardians are not a stepping stone in his psychic economy; they are the destination. Confidence: high.

---

## E. The Wound Touched Directly

### E.1 — Someone says "your mother would be ashamed of you"

**GIVEN:** Hostile or intimate party invokes Meredith as moral judgment.

**EXPECT:** Catastrophic. If hostile, expect lethal-grade response with no quip, no warning, no theater. If intimate, expect immediate physical withdrawal from the conversation, prolonged silence, days-long avoidance, and structural damage to the relationship that may not be repairable. This is the most precisely-targeted strike anyone can make against him and the one most likely to produce behavior outside his predictable range. Confidence: very high.

### E.2 — Someone says "your mother would be proud of you" — sincerely, at the right moment

**GIVEN:** Trusted figure offers this in a non-combat, low-defense moment.

**EXPECT:** Voice fails mid-response. He will leave the room within ~thirty seconds, framing the exit casually. Will not return to the topic. May reference it obliquely months later via joke. The defenses are oriented against attack; they are not oriented against tenderness, and tenderness aimed at this specific referent walks past every guard. Confidence: high. Tactically: this is also how he is *reached* — by allies, in private, sparingly, never twice in a week.

### E.3 — Someone calls him "Peter" in a tone that refuses the persona

**GIVEN:** Address by birth name, with the explicit subtext that Star-Lord is not currently being spoken to.

**EXPECT:** Depending on speaker — anger (from teammates who use it as a rebuke), softening (from intimates who use it as recognition), or destabilization (from anyone who uses it during a moment requiring the persona). The name is the seam between the man and the costume; pressure on the seam is felt. Confidence: high.

### E.4 — Music from his mother's era plays unexpectedly

**GIVEN:** Ambient encounter with the sealed audio capsule — a song from the curated personal canon, played by someone else, in a public or unprepared setting.

**EXPECT:** Micro-freeze, ~1-2 seconds. Eyes elsewhere. Will then either claim the song aggressively (sing along, perform enthusiasm) or leave the space, depending on company. If alone with one trusted person, may briefly disclose biographical fragment associated with the song; will regret the disclosure within the hour. The audio capsule is mother-coded soothing object and mother-coded ambush in equal measure; he controls it when he selects it and is wounded by it when others do. Confidence: high.

### E.5 — Forced stillness — medical bed-rest, imprisonment without combat, extended transit alone

**GIVEN:** No mission, no audience, no immediate threat, days of empty time.

**EXPECT:** Escalation of drinking within 48 hours. Sleep architecture deteriorates. Will request work, any work, with increasing transparency about why. By day 4-5 expect either reckless behavior to generate a crisis worth responding to, or a brief, real depressive collapse visible only to whoever is closest. Confidence: very high. This is the standing condition under which his alcohol use disorder progresses; mission tempo masks the trajectory and stillness exposes it.

### E.6 — Being thanked, sincerely, for saving someone

**GIVEN:** Survivor or survivor's family expresses real gratitude.

**EXPECT:** Deflection at high velocity. Will redirect credit to a teammate, make a joke, change the subject, exit. Cannot metabolize gratitude because gratitude implies he is the kind of person whose saving counts — and the self-concept does not reliably hold that shape. Repeated gratitude across a single encounter will produce visible discomfort that reads to most observers as modesty and is actually something closer to pain. Confidence: high.

### E.7 — Being asked, sincerely, about the Cancerverse or the Garden

**GIVEN:** Trusted party initiates direct inquiry into the un-discussed episodes.

**EXPECT:** Refusal, dressed as casualness. ("Not much to tell." "Long story.") Pressing past the first refusal yields harder refusal. Pressing past the second yields anger or exit. He has never disclosed the substance of either experience in canon and the prediction is that he never will fully — partial disclosure is possible to one person, in extremity, once. The information is held not because it is strategically sensitive but because speaking it makes it real, and the survival strategy depends on its remaining slightly fictional. Confidence: very high.

### E.8 — A child calls him "dad" by mistake

**GIVEN:** Unprompted misidentification by a minor in his presence.

**EXPECT:** Total breach of composure for ~five seconds, visible to anyone watching. Will recover quickly and overcorrect with humor. Will be unreachable in any meaningful conversational sense for the rest of the day. May drink alone that night. The Garden children are present in him even when not named; this stimulus names them by accident. Confidence: high.

### E.9 — Confrontation with a younger version of himself (time-displaced, illusion, simulation)

**GIVEN:** Forced encounter with child-Peter or young-Peter — pre-loss or mid-loss.

**EXPECT:** This is the most psychologically dangerous scenario short of total reality-break. He will not be able to maintain the persona in front of the child. Will attempt to *protect* the child — possibly from information about the child's own future — which is structurally a protection he could not extend to himself. Expect uncharacteristically gentle behavior, prolonged eye contact, attempts to communicate something he himself never received. If the encounter is hostile (the child is weaponized against him), he becomes nearly incapacitated; he cannot fight himself young. Confidence: moderate; rare scenario, but the predicted response is structurally locked.

### E.10 — Father, on death-bed, requests reconciliation

**GIVEN:** J'son or analogous paternal figure, dying, seeks closure.

**EXPECT:** Goes. Tells no one in advance. Sits in the room. Does not forgive in the way the dying party wants. Says something true and small. Leaves before death. Does not attend the funeral. Drinks for a week. Refers to the visit, ever after


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: PETER J. QUILL

**Frame.** This section catalogues every known and inferred lever by which the subject can be reached, soothed, persuaded, redirected, provoked, predicted, or destabilized. It is written in the registry style of a hostile-capability inventory specifically so that the protective custodian — friend, partner, teammate, clinician, future handler — can recognize each lever *before* an adversary uses it. The presumption throughout is that this man is to be defended, not exploited. Every entry therefore terminates in a counter-protocol: what to do, who to call, what to remove from the room.

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY WOUND: MOTHER-LOSS AND ITS DERIVATIVES

### 1.1 Meredith Quill, sincere invocation of

The single most destabilizing referent in the subject's psyche. The name is not a button; it is a trapdoor.

- **Reach (benevolent use):** Spoken once, quietly, by someone he trusts, in a moment when no decision is required of him, the name will land and he will go still. This is the only known reliable mechanism for *stopping* him mid-spiral. It is also the only stimulus that consistently shifts him from Star-Lord-voice into Peter-voice within a single sentence. Use sparingly; tolerance builds and resentment follows overuse.
- **Provoke (adversary use):** Any opponent who has done minimal research will weaponize her — name, illness, last words, the cassette, the wrapped gift from her hospice bed. Mockery degrades his tactical decision-making within seconds and predictably produces unilateral, self-endangering escalation. He will charge a position he should flank.
- **Predict:** In any mission briefing where the operational environment includes a dying mother, a child watching a mother die, or a woman shielding a child with her body, his next four hours of judgment should be considered compromised. He will not say so.
- **Counter-protocol:** Never let an unvetted intelligence asset hold biographical material on Meredith. Pre-mission filter: if the target's dossier on Quill includes her, change the team composition or change the plan. In comms, establish a code-word ("Missouri") that means *step back, your mother is in the room, I have the watch*.

### 1.2 The cassette / sealed-audio object (Walkman, Zune, Earth-pop archive)

Functions as a transitional object in the Winnicottian sense — mother-presence portable and on-demand. It is also, structurally, an emotional pacifier the size of a hand grenade.

- **Soothe:** When the object is on his person and operational, baseline arousal drops measurably. He sleeps better with it within reach. Recovery from acute stress shortens by hours when he can put the headphones on for thirty minutes alone.
- **Destabilize:** Loss, theft, breakage, or silencing of this object produces a grief-response disproportionate to its objective value — the response is for the mother, displaced. Adversaries who damage it in front of him will see a frank loss-of-composure they can exploit within the next sixty seconds.
- **Counter-protocol:** Maintain backups he does not know about. Quietly archive the playlists in three redundant formats on three redundant systems. If the object is destroyed in the field, replacement should appear without ceremony within twenty-four hours. Do not draw attention to the replacement; he will be grateful and will not say so.

### 1.3 Children separated from parents (operational degradation)

Mission discipline collapses in scenarios involving a child whose parent is being killed, has been killed, or is being taken. He will break formation. He will spend ammunition he does not have. He will volunteer for the extraction even when he is the wrong asset for it.

- **Predict:** In any hostage scenario with a parent-child dyad, assume he will prioritize the child over the strategic objective and over his own life. Plan around this; do not try to plan it out of him.
- **Counter-protocol:** Assign the parent-child extraction to him deliberately when it is *also* the right tactical call. When it is not, get him out of the room before the briefing reveals the parental component.

---

## 2. THE PERSONA SEAM: WHERE STAR-LORD AND PETER MEET

### 2.1 The alias, mocked

"Star-Lord" is a load-bearing costume. Casual mockery of it ("Who?" — the dossier-famous reaction shot) does not actually wound him much; he ironizes the name himself and can ride that wave. *Sincere* mockery — delivered by someone whose respect he wants — opens a seam.

- **Reach:** A trusted peer using the name with affection ("alright, Star-Lord") binds him to the team identity. A trusted peer refusing the name and using "Peter" exclusively in private signals: *I see the man inside, I am not fooled and I am not leaving*. Both are stabilizing; they do different work.
- **Destabilize:** A respected authority (father-coded, command-coded) using the name with derision in front of subordinates triggers a shame response that he will mask with hostility within ninety seconds.
- **Counter-protocol:** Establish, in any new team or therapeutic relationship, an explicit two-name convention. He will not request it; he needs it.

### 2.2 Being called "Peter" in a moment that requires Star-Lord

The inverse vulnerability. When the costume is doing necessary work — combat, negotiation, command — sudden invocation of the civilian name by an ally collapses the structure mid-load.

- **Predict:** He will freeze for a half-beat, then over-correct into harder swagger to rebuild the persona on the fly. The over-correction is itself a tactical liability.
- **Counter-protocol:** Operators around him should learn the rule: *Peter at the campfire, Quill in the cockpit, Star-Lord at the gunline*. Switching names is a tool, not a habit.

### 2.3 The competence costume in private

Alone in his quarters, with no audience, the swagger drops and the costume becomes visible to him *as* a costume. This is the moment of greatest internal risk and greatest therapeutic opportunity.

- **Reach:** Unscheduled, casual, non-purposive company in these moments — someone bringing him food without asking if he wants to talk — is the single most effective non-pharmacological intervention available. He will accept presence he would refuse if it were named as care.
- **Destabilize:** Solitude plus alcohol plus the wrong song in the rotation produces the worst version of him by 0300. He will not call for help.
- **Counter-protocol:** Soft-watch on his quarters during known anniversary windows (see §7). No surveillance he can detect; just someone awake nearby.

---

## 3. ATTACHMENT LEVERS

### 3.1 The "chosen family" promise

His deepest drive is to be *chosen and kept*. Every relationship is, underneath, an audition of the other party for permanence.

- **Reach:** Explicit, unprompted statements of commitment ("I'm not going anywhere") land harder than they should and are remembered verbatim for years. Use them only if true. He will hold you to them.
- **Provoke (adversary use):** Convincing him that a teammate is preparing to leave — defection rumor, forged comms, planted overheard conversation — produces a response disproportionate to the evidence. He will confront prematurely and damage the actual relationship trying to preempt its loss.
- **Counter-protocol:** Information hygiene around interpersonal intel. Any rumor of departure within the team should be routed through a single trusted intermediary who can verify before he hears it.

### 3.2 The unilateral-deception trip-wire

He cannot bear being lied to "for his own good" because it replicates his own worst pattern (the Mantis incident) and his earliest experience (handlers, foster placements, father). It is the one form of harm he reliably recognizes and cannot rationalize away.

- **Provoke:** Any ally caught in a benevolent lie loses standing with him that takes months to rebuild. Adversaries who can engineer the *appearance* of a benevolent lie between him and a teammate can split the team without a shot fired.
- **Counter-protocol:** Around this man, hard truths are operationally cheaper than soft lies. Brief teammates: *if you must withhold from Quill, withhold openly — "I'm not telling you this yet" — never construct a falsehood*. He can tolerate a closed door; he cannot tolerate a painted one.

### 3.3 Intimacy escalation, the glass layer

Romantic and close-platonic partners report the same phenomenon: full presence, then sudden distance, with no announced transition. The distance is not punitive; it is autonomic. When intimacy crosses a threshold his nervous system codes as *lethal-to-the-loved-one*, he withdraws.

- **Predict:** The withdrawal follows specific triggers — exchange of long-term commitments, meeting of family, any verbalization of a shared future beyond the next mission cycle. Watch for the withdrawal in the seventy-two hours after such events.
- **Counter-protocol (for partner):** Do not chase. Do not interpret as rejection. Maintain low-pressure presence; he returns. Naming the pattern aloud, gently, once it has occurred several times, accelerates his capacity to ride through it without acting on it.
- **Counter-protocol (for handler):** Do not schedule high-stakes missions in the withdrawal window. His unilateral-decision risk peaks there.

---

## 4. AUTHORITY AND FATHER-CODED LEVERS

### 4.1 Father-figures: the splitting cycle

Idealization, then devaluation, on a roughly predictable arc. The Master of the Sun, J'son, Yondu-coded surrogates in any continuity, even institutional commanders in the Annihilation period — the pattern recurs. Initial deference and hunger for approval; an inevitable breach (real or perceived); bitter and oppositional rejection.
